\section{Minimal Explicit Microscopic Coupling that Opens the Odd Extra-Carrier Route}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The \(JK\)-route has been reduced to a single frozen-harmonic overlap test, but that test is still data-blocked in the present conversation.
Therefore the honest forward-computable route is the explicit odd extra-carrier branch.

The minimal microscopic completion that opens this route is the addition of the odd Class-II carrier slot
\[
\gamma_O\,X_i^a\,\mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
\]

Once this slot is present, the odd reduced coefficient is no longer schematic:
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1,
\]
and the branch-level odd coefficient is
\[
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
\]

So the first explicit odd-channel opening mechanism is already fixed at operator level.

\section{1. Minimal one-mediator microscopic completion}

The minimal one-mediator working truncation that is capable of carrying both even and odd transverse sectors is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trunc}}
=
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_E X_i^a \mathcal E_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:minimal_one_mediator_with_odd}
\end{equation}

The new ingredient relative to the previously stalled routes is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:odd_slot_minimal}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal explicit microscopic odd extra-carrier coupling.

\section{2. Explicit odd carrier generated by the extra slot}

The explicit odd extra-carrier route gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_O(\theta)=\Tr(S_OM_O)=\cos\theta.
}
\label{eq:qO_cos_theta}
\end{equation}

Therefore the odd explicit carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:IO_explicit_again}
\end{equation}

Its induced tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VEO_again}
\end{equation}

Hence the local odd transverse density is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:bO_local_again}
\end{equation}

So the odd channel is locally present whenever
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0,
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0,
\qquad
\cos\theta(\xi)\not\equiv0.
\]

\section{3. Microscopic coefficient reading}

At operator level, the explicit odd route gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_operator_reading}
\end{equation}

If the shell basis is canonically normalized,
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_canonical}
\end{equation}

In the canonical transport-side explicit branch notation, the normalization layer is absorbed into the coefficient point, so one writes simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_transport_canonical}
\end{equation}

Thus the minimal odd microscopic coupling produces a nonzero odd coefficient already at one-mediator level whenever the mediator coupling pair \((\beta_X,\gamma_O)\) is nonzero and the overlap factor does not vanish.

\section{4. Reduced branch-level odd coefficient}

The explicit extra odd carrier has already been fully inserted into the reduced coefficient sheet:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:beta_reading_explicit}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:LambdaO_operator_reading} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:beta_operator_explicit}
\end{equation}

Under canonical shell normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:beta_canonical_explicit}
\end{equation}

So the odd coefficient is now reduced to a direct product of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the mediator-sector couplings \(\beta_X,\gamma_O\),
\item the heavy scale \(M_X^2\),
\item the microscopic odd overlap \(J_1\),
\item the geometric defect overlap \(I_c\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{5. Exact nonzero condition}

From \eqref{eq:beta_operator_explicit}, the odd transverse channel is nonzero if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,
\qquad
J_1\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0.
}
\label{eq:beta_nonzero_minimal_conditions}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in reduced reading form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0
\quad\text{and}\quad
I_c\neq0.
}
\label{eq:beta_nonzero_reduced}
\end{equation}

This is the first fully explicit branch-level odd-channel criterion available on the present data.

\section{6. Why this is the correct forward route}

The \(JK\)-route still requires unavailable frozen harmonics
\[
\bar A_G,\qquad B_G^{(E)}
\]
to evaluate its final sign test explicitly.
By contrast, the explicit odd extra-carrier route already gives the coefficient reading
\[
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c
\]
without needing those unavailable harmonics.

Therefore the microscopic odd frontier is no longer “whether an odd route exists.”
It is only the actual value/sign extraction of
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
\]

\section{Conclusion}

The minimal explicit microscopic coupling that opens the odd channel is the odd extra-carrier slot
\[
\boxed{
\gamma_O X_i^a\mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\]

Once this is added to the one-mediator branch, one gets
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\]

So the odd transverse channel is explicitly realizable at lowest order on the complete carrier route, and the remaining microscopic problem is only the actual sign/value of \(J_1\) (equivalently of \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\)).

\section{Final Summary}

The minimal explicit microscopic coupling that opens the odd extra-carrier route is
\[
\boxed{
\gamma_O X_i^a\mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\]

With this term included, the explicit odd carrier is
\[
\mathcal I_O=X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi,
\]
and the induced tangent transport block is
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
\]

The microscopic odd coefficient is read off as
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\]

Therefore the reduced odd transverse coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\]

In canonical normalization this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_c.
}
\]

Hence the exact minimal nonzero condition is
\[
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,\qquad
J_1\neq0,\qquad
I_c\neq0.
}
\]

So the odd route is no longer conceptually open.
It is explicitly available at one-mediator level, and the remaining microscopic frontier is only the actual value/sign of \(J_1\) (equivalently of \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\)).

\section{Exact Sign Convention for the Explicit Odd Coefficient}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The odd extra-carrier route is already fully inserted into the reduced coefficient sheet.
The relevant formulas are:

\[
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,I_{\theta,\cos},
\]
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1,
\]
and in canonical explicit normalization,
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
\]

Therefore the sign of \(\beta\) is completely fixed by the sign of the microscopic coupling product and the orientation/overlap factor.
There is no remaining structural ambiguity.

\section{1. Exact reduced odd coefficient}

The explicit extra odd carrier route gives the exact reduced dictionary
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:odd_sign_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Thus the odd coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,I_{\theta,\cos},
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:beta_exact_sign_start}
\end{equation}

At operator level, the one-mediator microscopic coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_operator_sign}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:LambdaO_operator_sign} into \eqref{eq:beta_exact_sign_start} yields the exact unabsorbed sign formula
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}.
}
\label{eq:beta_unabsorbed_sign}
\end{equation}

Since \(M_X^2>0\), its sign is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:sgn_beta_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}

This is the exact sign rule in the unabsorbed normalization.

\section{2. Canonical explicit normalization}

In the canonical explicit normalization one chooses
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
\]
Then the operator coefficient reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_canonical_unabsorbedJ1}
\end{equation}

If one keeps \(J_1\) explicit, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_{\theta,\cos},
}
\label{eq:beta_canonical_J1}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,J_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:sgn_beta_canonical_J1}
\end{equation}

If one instead absorbs \(J_1\) into the transport-side normalization, the notes give
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_{\theta,\cos}.
}
\label{eq:beta_canonical_absorbed}
\end{equation}
Hence the fully canonical sign rule is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:sgn_beta_canonical_absorbed}
\end{equation}

So the only difference between the two conventions is whether \(J_1\) is regarded as part of the coefficient or as part of the normalization bookkeeping.
The physical sign rule is unchanged.

\section{3. Branch decision and pure-even branch exclusion}

The notes also state that the current explicit witness branch is the pure-even one:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0.
}
\label{eq:pure_even_branch_again}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O=0,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:pure_even_beta_zero}
\end{equation}

So the pure-even explicit witness branch can never be used to read a nonzero odd coefficient.

To activate the odd channel one must move to a mixed transverse branch with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:gammaO_nonzero_branch}
\end{equation}

Once \(\gamma_O\neq0\), the odd coefficient is no longer structurally obstructed.
It is decided only by the sign of
\[
\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}
\]
(or \(\beta_X\gamma_O\,I_{\theta,\cos}\) in the fully absorbed canonical convention).

\section{4. Orientation convention for the defect overlap}

The overlap factor is
\[
I_{\theta,\cos}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

Its sign is not an additional dynamical mystery.
It depends on the chosen orientation of the defect coordinate \(\xi\) and on the orientation convention for the profile \(\theta(\xi)\).

Therefore one may adopt the \emph{canonical overlap orientation convention}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta,\cos}>0.
}
\label{eq:canonical_overlap_orientation}
\end{equation}

Under this convention, the sign rules simplify to

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\bigr)
}
\quad
\text{(unabsorbed normalization),}
\label{eq:sgn_beta_overlap_fixed_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,J_1\bigr)
}
\quad
\text{(canonical with explicit }J_1\text{),}
\label{eq:sgn_beta_overlap_fixed_J1}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\bigr)
}
\quad
\text{(fully absorbed canonical transport notation).}
\label{eq:sgn_beta_overlap_fixed_absorbed}
\end{equation}

This is a convention choice, not a theorem.
It is exactly the correct way to separate physical coupling signs from coordinate-orientation bookkeeping.

\section{5. Minimal nonzero and sign-stable criterion}

The notes already give the minimal nonzero criterion:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq 0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:min_nonzero_beta}
\end{equation}
and, in the unabsorbed operator normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_OJ_1\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:min_nonzero_beta_overlap}
\end{equation}

So the sign-stable odd branch is obtained once these nonvanishing conditions hold and the overlap orientation is fixed.

In particular, after choosing the canonical overlap orientation \(I_{\theta,\cos}>0\), the odd coefficient has a fixed sign as soon as
\[
\beta_X,\qquad \gamma_O,\qquad J_1
\]
have fixed signs.

Thus the sign problem is no longer structural.
It is now only a bookkeeping choice plus the microscopic signs of the couplings.

\section{Conclusion}

The exact odd-coefficient sign formula is
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
}
\]

In canonical explicit normalization:
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_{\theta,\cos},
\qquad
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,J_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
}
\]

If \(J_1\) is also absorbed into the transport-side normalization, then
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_{\theta,\cos},
\qquad
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
}
\]

After fixing the canonical defect-orientation convention \(I_{\theta,\cos}>0\), these reduce to the simplest branch sign rules
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\bigr),
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\bigr)
}
\]
in the fully absorbed canonical transport notation.

Therefore the odd-channel route is now completely sign-closed.
The current pure-even branch has \(\gamma_O=0\) and hence \(\beta=0\).
The next actual branch must satisfy \(\gamma_O\neq0\), after which the sign of \(\beta\) is fixed entirely by the microscopic coupling signs and the chosen overlap orientation convention.

\section{Final Summary}

The explicit odd extra-carrier route gives the exact odd coefficient
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos},
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

Therefore the exact sign rule is
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}\bigr).
\]

In canonical explicit normalization,
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_{\theta,\cos},
\]
and if \(J_1\) is absorbed into the transport normalization,
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_{\theta,\cos}.
\]

Thus the remaining sign choice is only the overlap-orientation convention for \(I_{\theta,\cos}\).
After fixing \(I_{\theta,\cos}>0\), one gets
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\,C_OJ_1\bigr),
\]
or, in the fully absorbed canonical notation,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(\beta_X\gamma_O\bigr).
\]

The current pure-even explicit witness branch has
\[
\gamma_O=0,
\]
so it necessarily gives
\[
\beta=0.
\]

Therefore the next actual branch must be a mixed transverse branch with \(\gamma_O\neq0\), after which the sign of \(\beta\) is completely fixed by microscopic coupling signs and the overlap-orientation convention.

\section{Mixed Transverse Branch Upgrade: First Explicit Branch with \texorpdfstring{$\beta\neq0$}{beta neq 0}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The pure-even explicit witness branch
\[
\gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0
\]
necessarily gives
\[
\beta=0,
\]
so it must be abandoned if the goal is to read the odd coefficient.

The correct next branch is the mixed transverse branch
\[
T_O\neq0
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0.
\]

The simplest canonical mixed sample is
\[
T_E=T_O=1.
\]

On this branch, the reduced symbol already becomes an explicit anisotropic Dirac symbol with both even and odd transverse components turned on.

\section{1. Exact mixed-branch master symbol}

The exact mixed-branch reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:mixed_master_symbol}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
\beta_X I_\theta T_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
\beta_X I_\theta T_O.
}
\label{eq:mixed_coeff_sheet}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit overlap values
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:mixed_overlap_values}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:mixed_explicit_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Thus the odd channel is turned on exactly when
\[
\boxed{
T_O\neq0
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0.
}
\]

\section{2. Canonical minimal mixed sample}

Now choose the simplest canonical mixed branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_mixed_choice}
\end{equation}

Then \eqref{eq:mixed_explicit_coeffs} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_mixed_sample}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_mixed_sample}
\end{equation}

The transverse resultant amplitude is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}=\sqrt2.
}
\label{eq:Rperp_mixed_sample}
\end{equation}

The corresponding branch angle is
\[
T_E=R_\perp\cos\varphi,\qquad
T_O=R_\perp\sin\varphi,
\]
so for \(T_E=T_O=1\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\qquad
\frac{\beta}{\alpha}=\tan\varphi=1.
}
\label{eq:phi_pi4}
\end{equation}

The document also gives the corresponding explicit overlap factor
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:Delta00_mixed_sample}
\end{equation}

Therefore this branch is the first explicit mixed transverse sample on which the odd coefficient is genuinely nonzero.

\section{3. Sign rule on the canonical mixed branch}

From \eqref{eq:alpha_beta_mixed_sample},
\[
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Hence, on the canonical mixed sample \(T_E=T_O=1\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\alpha
=
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa).
}
\label{eq:sign_rule_canonical_mixed}
\end{equation}

So once the defect orientation convention fixes the sign of \(\theta_0\kappa\), the sign of the odd coefficient is determined entirely by the sign of \(\beta_X\).

In particular, if one adopts the standard positive-defect convention
\[
\theta_0\kappa>0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X).
}
\label{eq:beta_sign_positive_defect}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Honest status after the mixed-branch upgrade}

The mixed transverse branch upgrade does \emph{not} mean that the full microscopic PDE has already been finally derived.
What is closed is the reduced branch-level symbol and its coefficient reading.

The final unconditional microscopic PDE is still open, and the remaining frontier is still
\[
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

So the honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the odd coefficient is now explicitly readable on the mixed transverse branch,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic coefficient extraction from the complete TECT operator remains open.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The pure-even witness branch
\[
\gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0
\]
necessarily gives
\[
\beta=0.
\]

Therefore the correct next branch is the mixed transverse branch
\[
\boxed{
T_O\neq0
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0.
}
\]

The exact mixed-branch coefficient sheet is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

For the simplest canonical mixed sample
\[
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
}
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta}{\alpha}=1.
}
\]

Thus this is the first explicit branch on which the odd coefficient is genuinely turned on.

Its sign rule is
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa).
}
\]

Under the standard convention \(\theta_0\kappa>0\),
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\beta=-\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X).
}
\]

So the mixed transverse branch upgrade closes the branch-level odd coefficient reading, while the final microscopic PDE coefficient extraction still remains open.

\section{Mixed Odd-Active Branch: Exact Matching Layer to the Finite Microscopic Extraction Chain}

\section{Short explanation}

The mixed transverse branch is no longer a structural guess.
Its reduced symbol is already fixed exactly, and the next legitimate task is to connect it back to the finite microscopic extraction chain
\[
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

The cleanest first odd-active sample is the canonical mixed choice
\[
T_E=T_O=1.
\]
The correct next layer is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item write the exact target coefficient point for this branch,
\item translate it into target conditions on the projected Bloch derivative matrices,
\item attach the branch-consistent same-shell support inequality,
\item state honestly what remains finite insertion rather than open structure.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Exact mixed-branch target coefficient sheet}

The exact mixed-branch reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:mixed_target_symbol}
\end{equation}

Using the exact overlap factors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:mixed_target_overlaps}
\end{equation}
the reduced coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:mixed_target_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:mixed_target_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

The exact nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
R_\perp:=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}>0.
}
\label{eq:mixed_target_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Canonical mixed sample}

Choose the first odd-active canonical mixed sample
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_mixed_sample}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:canonical_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:canonical_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Moreover
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta}{\alpha}=1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_sample_data}
\end{equation}

So this is the first explicit odd-active reduced coefficient point.

\section{3. Exact matching back to the projected Bloch derivative matrices}

Let
\[
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
M_i:=P_*K_iP_*.
\]
Then the microscopic frontier is to compute these \(M_i\) explicitly from the complete operator and verify that they match the mixed-branch target.

In the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), define
\[
M_\parallel:=\hat n^iM_i,
\qquad
M_1:=e_1^iM_i,
\qquad
M_2:=e_2^iM_i.
\]

The mixed-branch target matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{\mathrm{target}}
=
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Mpar_target}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_1^{\mathrm{target}}
=
\alpha\,\sigma_1+\beta\,\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2^{\mathrm{target}}
=
\alpha\,\sigma_2-\beta\,\sigma_1.
}
\label{eq:M12_target}
\end{equation}

Therefore on the canonical mixed sample \(T_E=T_O=1\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_1^{\mathrm{target}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,(\sigma_1+\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:M1_target_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_2^{\mathrm{target}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,(\sigma_2-\sigma_1).
}
\label{eq:M2_target_canonical}
\end{equation}

So the finite microscopic extraction problem is now exactly the finite matrix-matching problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_\parallel P_* \stackrel{?}{=}
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Kpar_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_1P_* \stackrel{?}{=}
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,(\sigma_1+\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:K1_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_2P_* \stackrel{?}{=}
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,(\sigma_2-\sigma_1).
}
\label{eq:K2_match}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in trace-reading form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel)
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:trace_lambda_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2)
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:trace_alpha_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2)
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:trace_beta_match}
\end{equation}

This is the exact mixed-branch microscopic target.

\section{4. Branch-consistent same-shell support criterion}

The pure-even same-shell benchmark is already known, and for the canonical mixed branch the branch-consistent lift is also already fixed.

For
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\]
the effective same-shell correction strength becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:aT_mixed}
\end{equation}

The corresponding overlap package is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:S_mixed_package}
\end{equation}

Hence the correct branch-consistent sufficient same-shell support condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_support_criterion}
\end{equation}

So the support-side problem is no longer conceptual either.
It is a finite insertion problem for the mixed same-shell constants
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},
\quad
L_+^{TT},\quad
L_-^{TT},\quad
L_0^{TT},\quad
C_+^{TT},\quad
C_-^{TT},\quad
C_m^{TT}.
\]

\section{5. Honest current status}

The mixed-branch coefficient sheet is exact.
The branch-consistent same-shell support inequality is also exact.
The remaining frontier is still finite insertion, not conceptual structure.

What is \emph{not} yet closed is the unconditional extraction from the final complete TECT operator.
So the honest status remains:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{reduced mixed-branch odd reading is closed,}
\qquad
\text{full microscopic extraction remains open.}
}
\label{eq:honest_status_mixed}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The mixed odd-active branch has now been matched to the exact finite microscopic target.

The canonical mixed sample \(T_E=T_O=1\) fixes
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
\]
and therefore fixes the target projected derivative matrices
\[
M_\parallel^{\mathrm{target}}=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1^{\mathrm{target}}=\alpha(\sigma_1+\sigma_2),
\qquad
M_2^{\mathrm{target}}=\alpha(\sigma_2-\sigma_1).
\]

So the full microscopic frontier is now a finite matrix-matching and same-shell insertion problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The mixed transverse branch with
\[
T_O\neq0
\]
is the correct odd-active upgrade of the pure-even witness branch.
For the canonical mixed sample
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\]
the exact reduced coefficient point is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
\]
with
\[
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2}.
\]

Therefore the exact microscopic extraction target becomes
\[
P_*K_\parallel P_* \stackrel{?}{=} \lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
P_*K_1P_* \stackrel{?}{=} \alpha(\sigma_1+\sigma_2),
\qquad
P_*K_2P_* \stackrel{?}{=} \alpha(\sigma_2-\sigma_1).
\]

The corresponding branch-consistent same-shell sufficient condition is
\[
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
\]

Thus the mixed odd-active branch is no longer structurally open.
It is now reduced to:
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite projected Bloch-derivative matching}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite same-shell constant insertion}.
}
\]

What remains open is not the reduced branch logic, but the final unconditional microscopic extraction from the complete TECT operator.

\section{Exact Same-Shell Support Sheet for the Canonical Mixed Odd-Active Branch}

\section{Goal}

We now fix the first explicit odd-active mixed branch by
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4}.
\]

The reduced coefficient point is already exact:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa.
\]

So the nontrivial remaining support-side problem is not structural.
It is the same-shell non-enriched benchmark on this mixed branch.

\section{1. Exact mixed same-shell block}

The pure-even same-shell block was
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p)&m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)}&d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
d_\pm(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(\pm p)-a_K\mathcal S_{\pm\pm}^{EE}(p),
\qquad
m(p)=B_{z_0}(p)-a_K\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p).
\]

The branch-consistent mixed uplift is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_+^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:mixed_dp_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_-^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(-p)-a_T\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:mixed_dm_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(T)}(p)
=
B_{z_0}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:mixed_mp_exact}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:aT_exact}
\end{equation}

So the mixed same-shell benchmark remains a \(2\times2\) Hermitian problem, but with the \(EE\)-family replaced by the mixed \(TT\)-family.

\section{2. Canonical \texorpdfstring{$\pi/4$}{pi/4} overlap package}

For the canonical mixed branch
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\]
the overlap family is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:Sab_pi4_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\max\Bigl\{
|\mathcal S_{++}^{(\pi/4)}(0)|,\ 
|\mathcal S_{--}^{(\pi/4)}(0)|,\ 
|\mathcal S_{+-}^{(\pi/4)}(0)|
\Bigr\},
}
\label{eq:Sdiag_pi4_def}
\end{equation}
or, if one adopts the symmetric locked-core reduction used in the notes, the same object may be written as the common diagonal benchmark extracted from the mixed family
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi).
\]

Thus for the canonical branch the coefficient entering the support inequality is not a new unknown function class; it is the explicit \(\pi/4\) combination of the already known \(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) overlap families.

\section{3. Exact small-\texorpdfstring{$p$}{p} drift budgets}

Differentiate the mixed same-shell family at \(p=0\). The direct core drift is unchanged:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
a_{-,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
b_i^{\mathrm{dir}}=0.
}
\label{eq:adir_mixed}
\end{equation}

Now define the mixed derivative budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p;\varphi)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p;\varphi)\right|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:ellpm_mixed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p;\varphi)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:ell0_mixed}
\end{equation}

Then the full mixed drift coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{(T)}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{+,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:aplus_mixed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{(T)}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{-,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:aminus_mixed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i^{(T)}
=
-a_T\ell_{0,i}^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:b_mixed}
\end{equation}

Define the norm-level budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:Lpm0_mixed}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
}
\label{eq:Aplus_bound_mixed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_-^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
}
\label{eq:Aminus_bound_mixed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B^{(T)}
\le a_TL_0^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:B_bound_mixed}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact mixed-branch small-\texorpdfstring{$p$}{p} error budget}

Introduce the quadratic remainder constants
\[
C_+^{TT},\qquad C_-^{TT},\qquad C_m^{TT}.
\]
Then the mixed-branch small-\(p\) error satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{(T)}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{(T)}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{(T)}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:eps_smallp_mixed}
\end{equation}

For the canonical \(\pi/4\) branch, this is simply
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
=
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}\Big|_{\varphi=\pi/4}.
\]

\section{5. Exact branch-consistent support criterion}

Exactly parallel to the pure-even case, the branch-consistent mixed same-shell sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_T\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\label{eq:support_mixed_general}
\end{equation}

Substituting
\[
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\]
and specializing to \(\varphi=\pi/4\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:support_mixed_pi4}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the scalar-only locked-core form used in the notes,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:support_scalaronly_pi4}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest exact support-side inequality currently available for the first odd-active branch.

\section{6. What is still not inserted}

The notes are explicit that the following quantities are still not inserted numerically:
\begin{equation}

\section{1. Exact mixed same-shell support sheet}

For the canonical mixed branch
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},

the branch-consistent transverse overlap family is
\begin{equation}

\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:pi4_overlap_sheet}
\end{equation}

The same-shell block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_+^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_-^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(-p)-a_T\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(T)}(p)
=
B_{z_0}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p),
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the mixed drift budgets
\[
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(0),
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(0),
\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(0),
\]
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_L_budget}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{(T)}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{(T)}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{(T)}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2},
}
\label{eq:mixed_eps_sheet}
\end{equation}
with
\[
A_+^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
\]
\[
A_-^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
\]
\[
B^{(T)}\le a_TL_0^{TT}.
\]

Therefore the exact branch-consistent same-shell sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:final_same_shell_support}
\end{equation}

So the mixed same-shell side is reduced completely to the seven explicit finite constants

\section{2. Exact mixed-block transverse audit sheet}

The background-dependent Hessian transport kernel has already been reduced to the blocks
\[
TT,\quad TD,\quad DT,\quad DD,
\]
with universal one-derivative form
\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+\cdots,
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}:=\Pi_Q\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\Pi_Q.
\]

The invariant projectors are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
}
\label{eq:EO_projectors_audit}
\end{equation}

At the sharp minimal mixed-block stage,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT})\Pi_Q,
}
\end{equation}
and the leading transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\label{eq:eo_tddt_sheet}
\end{equation}

In the sharp current reading,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_0^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:LambdaEO_microsheet}
\end{equation}
or more generally
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaEO_fullsum}
\end{equation}

The conservative currently supported truncation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\approx0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\approx \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:conservative_mixed_audit}
\end{equation}

So the exact remaining cancellation test is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{

:=
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)}+\cdots,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
:=
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}+\cdots.
}
\end{equation}

Then the actual transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_cancellation_form}
\end{equation}

Thus the witness survives provided the mixed-block correction does not cancel the explicit \(K\)-sector pair:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\neq -e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\neq -o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:no_cancellation_criterion}
\end{equation}

A stronger sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:strong_survival_criterion}
\end{equation}

Under this condition the signs of \(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) are inherited from the explicit \(K\)-sector pair.

\section{Audit A: exact reduction of the mixed same-shell support problem}

The exact mixed-branch same-shell overlap package is
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
\qquad a,b\in\{+,-\}.
\]
For the canonical branch
\[
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+

+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
}
\]

Now assume the small-\(p\) drift coefficients are defined by the corresponding Taylor data of the same-shell package:
\[
\ell_{+,i}^{XY},\quad
\ell_{-,i}^{XY},\quad
\ell_{0,i}^{XY},
\qquad
C_+^{XY},\quad
C_-^{XY},\quad
C_m^{XY},
\qquad XY\in\{EE,OO,EO\}.
\]
Then linearity of differentiation gives the exact mixed formulas
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{+,i}^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{-,i}^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{0,i}^{EO},
}
\]
and likewise
\[
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
=
\frac12 C_+^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_+^{OO}
+
C_+^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_-^{TT}
=
\frac12 C_-^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_-^{OO}
+
C_-^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
=
\frac12 C_m^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}.
}
\]

Hence the seven missing mixed same-shell constants are reduced exactly to the already-separated
\(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) data:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},
\ L_+^{TT},\ L_-^{TT},\ L_0^{TT},\ C_+^{TT},\ C_-^{TT},\ C_m^{TT}
}
\]
with
\[
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i |\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i |\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i |\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
\]

At the norm level, one always has the rigorous upper bounds
\[
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12 L_+^{EE}
+
\frac12 L_+^{OO}
+
L_+^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
L_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12 L_-^{EE}
+
\frac12 L_-^{OO}
+
L_-^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
L_0^{TT}
\le
\frac12 L_0^{EE}
+
\frac12 L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO}.
}
\]
If all coefficients are sign-coherent in the chosen basis, these may sharpen to equalities, but the inequalities are the honest theorem-safe form.

Therefore the mixed same-shell support condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\right)
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\]
Moreover,
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{TT}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{TT}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{TT}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2},
\]
with
\[
A_+^{TT}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}L_+^{TT},
\]
\[
A_-^{TT}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}L_-^{TT},
\]
\[
B^{TT}
\le
\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}L_0^{TT}.
\]

So Audit A is no longer a conceptual problem.
It is exactly the finite insertion of the \(EE/OO/EO\) Taylor data into the formulas above.

\section{Audit B: exact reduction of the mixed-block transverse cancellation problem}

The exact remaining mixed-block corrections are
\[
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]
Using the invariant projector functionals on the projected one-derivative kernels,
\[
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\]
one has the exact blockwise identities
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{AB}\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{AB}\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
}
\]
with \(AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}\).

The actual transverse coefficient point is therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\]

There are then three logically distinct sufficient criteria:

\paragraph{Criterion B1: componentwise sign-preserving criterion.}
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\]
This preserves the nonvanishing of each component separately.

\paragraph{Criterion B2: Euclidean noncancellation criterion.}
Define
\[
v_K:=
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)},o_{0;K}^{(1)}\bigr),
\qquad
v_{\mathrm{mix}}:=
\bigl(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\|v_{\mathrm{mix}}\|_2<\|v_K\|_2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
v_K+v_{\mathrm{mix}}\neq(0,0).
}
\]
This is weaker than componentwise sign preservation, but sharper as a survival test for
\((\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0)\).

\paragraph{Criterion B3: exact cancellation test.}
The only actual failure condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}=-e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}=-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\]
So once the five mixed blocks are explicitly projected, the transverse audit is completely decided.

\section{Final coefficient point after the two audits}

After Audit A and Audit B, the final microscopic coefficient point is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
}
\]

Thus the project is reduced to the following exact finite checklist:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the \(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) same-shell Taylor packages;
\item assemble
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},\
\ell_{\pm,i}^{TT},\
\ell_{0,i}^{TT},\
C_+^{TT},\
C_-^{TT},\
C_m^{TT};
\]
\item evaluate the support inequality;
\item project the five mixed blocks
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD
\]
through \(\mathfrak P_E,\mathfrak P_O\);
\item compare the result against the explicit \(K\)-sector vector.
\end{enumerate}

No new conceptual theorem is needed beyond this point.
Only finite microscopic insertion remains.

\section{Final Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Current stage: the mixed odd-active branch is structurally closed,}
}
\]
but the final microscopic coefficient point still depends on exactly two finite audits.

For the canonical mixed branch
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\]
the branch-level reduced coefficients are already fixed.

The first remaining audit is the mixed same-shell support insertion.
Its exact overlap package is
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO},
\]
so the missing seven constants are reducible to the \(EE/OO/EO\) Taylor data.

The second remaining audit is the mixed-block transverse cancellation problem:
\[
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]
The actual transverse pair is
\[
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
\]

Hence the program is no longer waiting on a new mechanism.
It is reduced to a finite microscopic insertion-and-comparison problem.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Immediate next step: assemble the \(TT\) seven-constant package from \(EE/OO/EO\),}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{then project }TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\text{ to compute }(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}).
}
\]
