\section{Exact Closure of Audit A and Sharp Execution Order for Audit B}

\section{Current stage}

The reduced mixed odd-active branch is already fixed at the branch level by
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\]
and the remaining microscopic work is reduced to exactly two finite audits:
the mixed same-shell support insertion and the mixed-block transverse cancellation audit.

\section{1. Exact mixed same-shell package}

The branch-consistent mixed same-shell overlap family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
}
\label{eq:A1_STT_general}
\end{equation}
for \(a,b\in\{+,-\}\).

For the canonical mixed branch \(\varphi=\pi/4\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:A1_STT_pi4}
\end{equation}

The same-shell correction strength is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T
=
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(T_E^2+T_O^2)
=
\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:A1_aT}
\end{equation}

The mixed same-shell block is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_+^{(T)}(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:A1_dplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_-^{(T)}(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(-p)-a_T\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:A1_dminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(T)}(p)=B_{z_0}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p).
}
\label{eq:A1_m}
\end{equation}

Under the valley-symmetric diagonal subcase,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
:=
\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(0)=\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(0),
}
\label{eq:A1_Sdiag}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A1_Sdiag_pi4}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact first-derivative vectors}

Define the mixed first-derivative vectors by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:A1_ell_def}
\end{equation}

By linearity of differentiation and \eqref{eq:A1_STT_pi4},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{+,i}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A1_ell_plus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{-,i}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A1_ell_minus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{0,i}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A1_ell_zero}
\end{equation}

Now define the norm package
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}:=\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}:=\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}:=\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:A1_L_def}
\end{equation}

These are not independent constants. They satisfy the rigorous bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_+^{EE}
+
\frac12L_+^{OO}
+
L_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A1_Lplus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_-^{EE}
+
\frac12L_-^{OO}
+
L_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A1_Lminus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_0^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_0^{EE}
+
\frac12L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A1_L0_bound}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Important honesty point.}
The vector identities \eqref{eq:A1_ell_plus}--\eqref{eq:A1_ell_zero} are exact.
The norm formulas \eqref{eq:A1_Lplus_bound}--\eqref{eq:A1_L0_bound} are, in general, only upper bounds.

\section{3. Exact second-derivative tensors and honest \(C\)-constants}

Define the Hessian tensors
\begin{equation}
H^{TT}_{+,ij}:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
H^{TT}_{-,ij}:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
H^{TT}_{0,ij}:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
\label{eq:A1_Hessian_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{TT}_{+,ij}
=
\frac12H^{EE}_{+,ij}
+
\frac12H^{OO}_{+,ij}
+
H^{EO}_{+,ij},
}
\label{eq:A1_Hplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{TT}_{-,ij}
=
\frac12H^{EE}_{-,ij}
+
\frac12H^{OO}_{-,ij}
+
H^{EO}_{-,ij},
}
\label{eq:A1_Hminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{TT}_{0,ij}
=
\frac12H^{EE}_{0,ij}
+
\frac12H^{OO}_{0,ij}
+
H^{EO}_{0,ij}.
}
\label{eq:A1_H0}
\end{equation}

Now define valid quadratic Taylor remainder constants by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le\rho}\|\nabla_p^2 d_+^{(T)}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
C_-^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le\rho}\|\nabla_p^2 d_-^{(T)}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},
}
\label{eq:A1_Cpm_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le\rho}\|\nabla_p^2 m^{(T)}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
}
\label{eq:A1_Cm_def}
\end{equation}

Because these are supremum bounds, the honest branch-consistent estimates are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12 C_+^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_+^{OO}
+
C_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A1_Cplus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12 C_-^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_-^{OO}
+
C_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A1_Cminus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
\le
\frac12 C_m^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A1_Cm_bound}
\end{equation}

Again, these are generally sufficient bounds, not exact equalities.

\section{4. Mixed-branch drift budget}

The mixed drift coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{TT}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\,\ell_{+,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A1_aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{TT}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\,\ell_{-,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A1_aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i^{TT}
=
-a_T\,\ell_{0,i}^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:A1_b}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+^{TT}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A1_Aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_-^{TT}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A1_Aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B^{TT}\le a_TL_0^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:A1_B}
\end{equation}

Therefore the small-\(p\) budget satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{TT}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{TT}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{TT}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:A1_eps}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final exact form of Audit A}

The sharp mixed same-shell sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)},
}
\label{eq:A1_support_final}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO},
\]
and with \(L_\pm^{TT},L_0^{TT},C_\pm^{TT},C_m^{TT}\) given by the exact/bound formulas above.

Thus Audit A is completely reduced to the explicit insertion of the already-separated
\(EE/OO/EO\) overlap data.

\section{6. Sharp execution order for Audit B}

The exact mixed transverse coefficient routing is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:B1_exactsum}
\end{equation}

But the structurally principal source is \(TD+DT\), while \(OD,DO,DD\) are residual corrections.
Hence define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\Bigl(
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:B1_vpr}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
:=
\Bigl(
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:B1_rrem}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=v_{\mathrm{pr}}+r_{\mathrm{rem}}.
}
\label{eq:B1_split}
\end{equation}

Therefore the sharp execution order is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \(TD+DT\) exactly and obtain \(v_{\mathrm{pr}}\);
\item only then compute or bound \(OD+DO+DD\) as \(r_{\mathrm{rem}}\);
\item conclude noncancellation from a dominance test.
\end{enumerate}

Two useful sufficient criteria are:

\paragraph{Componentwise strong criterion.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)}|
<
|e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)}|,
}
\label{eq:B1_compE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}|
<
|o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:B1_compO}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Euclidean dominance criterion.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|r_{\mathrm{rem}}\|_2<\|v_{\mathrm{pr}}\|_2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:B1_Euclid}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Final populated coefficient point}

Once Audit A and Audit B are inserted,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:final_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:final_ab}
\end{equation}
with
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=v_{\mathrm{pr}}+r_{\mathrm{rem}}.
\]

So the remaining frontier is now purely finite:
\[
\boxed{
\text{assemble the }TT\text{ support package, then evaluate }TD+DT\text{ before all residual blocks.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The mixed odd-active branch is already structurally fixed.
The same-shell support audit is now reduced to the canonical mixed package
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
\]
which at \(\varphi=\pi/4\) becomes
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}.
\]

The diagonal and first-derivative data satisfy exact linear relations:
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO},
\]
\[
\ell_{\bullet}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{\bullet}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{\bullet}^{OO}
+
\ell_{\bullet}^{EO}.
\]

The norm constants \(L_\bullet^{TT}\) are therefore bounded by triangle inequalities,
while the quadratic remainder constants \(C_\bullet^{TT}\) are honest supremum bounds,
not exact linear identities in general.

Hence Audit A is fully reduced to finite insertion of the separated
\(EE/OO/EO\) overlap data.

For Audit B, the exact coefficient routing is
\[
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]
But the structurally principal source is \(TD+DT\), so the sharp execution order is
\[
(TD+DT)\ \text{first},
\qquad
(OD+DO+DD)\ \text{as residual correction second}.
\]

Therefore the project is now reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) assemble }(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},L_+^{TT},L_-^{TT},L_0^{TT},C_+^{TT},C_-^{TT},C_m^{TT}),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(ii) compute }v_{\mathrm{pr}}=(TD+DT)\text{ and only then add the residual correction }r_{\mathrm{rem}}.
}
\]

No new structural theorem is needed beyond this point.
Only finite microscopic insertion remains.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Audit A Closure: Exact Canonical \(TT\) Seven-Constant Package}

\section{Current stage}

For the canonical mixed odd-active branch,
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\qquad
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2},
\]
the same-shell benchmark remains a \(2\times2\) Hermitian problem, but with the pure-even
\(EE\) overlap family replaced by the mixed \(TT\) overlap family.

The key point is that the mixed overlap family is not new data.
It is assembled linearly from the already separated \(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) packages.

\section{1. Exact canonical mixed overlap family}

The mixed same-shell overlap family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:TT_master_family}
\end{equation}

At the canonical mixed branch \(\varphi=\pi/4\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:TT_pi4_family}
\end{equation}

Therefore the diagonal same-shell constant is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:TT_Sdiag_exact}
\end{equation}

This is an exact identity, not a bound.

\section{2. Exact first-derivative vectors}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:TT_ell_def}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:TT_pi4_family}, differentiation is linear, hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{+,i}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:TT_ell_plus_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{-,i}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:TT_ell_minus_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{0,i}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:TT_ell_zero_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus the derivative vectors are also exact linear combinations.

\section{3. Norm-level constants \(L_+^{TT},L_-^{TT},L_0^{TT}\)}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i |\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i |\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i |\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:TT_L_def}
\end{equation}

These are generally not exact linear combinations, because norms do not distribute linearly.
The honest theorem-level statement is the triangle-inequality bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12 L_+^{EE}
+
\frac12 L_+^{OO}
+
L_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:TT_Lplus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12 L_-^{EE}
+
\frac12 L_-^{OO}
+
L_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:TT_Lminus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_0^{TT}
\le
\frac12 L_0^{EE}
+
\frac12 L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:TT_L0_bound}
\end{equation}

If the three contributing vectors are sign/phase aligned in the chosen basis, these bounds can sharpen to equalities, but that is an additional branch-specific property and must not be assumed by default.

\section{4. Honest second-derivative package and \(C\)-constants}

The \(C\)-constants are quadratic Taylor-remainder bounds, not raw second derivatives.
So the correct object is the Hessian/supremum package.

Define the Hessian tensors
\begin{equation}
H^{TT}_{+,ij}(p):=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}d_+^{(T)}(p),
\qquad
H^{TT}_{-,ij}(p):=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}d_-^{(T)}(p),
\qquad
H^{TT}_{m,ij}(p):=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}m^{(T)}(p).
\label{eq:TT_Hessians}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|H^{TT}_{+}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
C_-^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|H^{TT}_{-}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
C_m^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|H^{TT}_{m}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
}
\label{eq:TT_C_def}
\end{equation}

Because the \(TT\) overlap family is linear in \(EE/OO/EO\), the Hessian tensors are also linear in those three sectors.
However, after taking operator norms and suprema, the correct general statement is again an upper bound:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12 C_+^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_+^{OO}
+
C_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:TT_Cplus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12 C_-^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_-^{OO}
+
C_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:TT_Cminus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
\le
\frac12 C_m^{EE}
+
\frac12 C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:TT_Cm_bound}
\end{equation}

So the \(C\)-package is controlled, but generally not by exact equality.

\section{5. Drift coefficients and norm budgets}

The direct locked-core contribution is unchanged:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
a_{-,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
b_i^{\mathrm{dir}}=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_direct_drift}
\end{equation}

The mixed-branch full derivative coefficients are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{(T)}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{+,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:TT_aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{(T)}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{-,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:TT_aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i^{(T)}
=
-a_T\ell_{0,i}^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:TT_b}
\end{equation}

Hence the norm-level budgets satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
}
\label{eq:TT_Aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_-^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
}
\label{eq:TT_Aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B^{(T)}\le a_TL_0^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:TT_B}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Explicit \(TT\) seven-constant table}

The canonical \(TT\) seven-constant package is therefore

\[
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{constant} & \text{status} & \text{canonical formula at }\varphi=\pi/4 \\[1mm]
\hline
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
& \text{exact}
&
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\\[2mm]
L_+^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
L_+^{TT}\le \frac12L_+^{EE}+\frac12L_+^{OO}+L_+^{EO}
\\[2mm]
L_-^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
L_-^{TT}\le \frac12L_-^{EE}+\frac12L_-^{OO}+L_-^{EO}
\\[2mm]
L_0^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
L_0^{TT}\le \frac12L_0^{EE}+\frac12L_0^{OO}+L_0^{EO}
\\[2mm]
C_+^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
C_+^{TT}\le \frac12C_+^{EE}+\frac12C_+^{OO}+C_+^{EO}
\\[2mm]
C_-^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
C_-^{TT}\le \frac12C_-^{EE}+\frac12C_-^{OO}+C_-^{EO}
\\[2mm]
C_m^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
C_m^{TT}\le \frac12C_m^{EE}+\frac12C_m^{OO}+C_m^{EO}
\end{array}
}
\]
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:TT_7constant_table}
\end{equation}

This is the honest fully reduced form of Audit A.

\section{7. Final mixed same-shell support inequality}

The mixed-branch same-shell small-\(p\) drift budget obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{(T)}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{(T)}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{(T)}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:TT_eps}
\end{equation}

Hence the final branch-consistent sufficient support condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_T\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\label{eq:TT_support_final}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2},
\]
this is equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\label{eq:TT_support_final_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{8. What remains after Audit A}

After \eqref{eq:TT_7constant_table} and \eqref{eq:TT_support_final_beta}, Audit A is no longer open structurally.

It is reduced to the explicit finite insertion of the three already separated packages:
\[
(EE),\qquad (OO),\qquad (EO).
\]

So the next nonredundant step is to evaluate the principal transverse mixed-block source
\[
TD+DT
\]
before the residual correction blocks
\[
OD,\quad DO,\quad DD.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

For the canonical mixed odd-active branch, the same-shell \(TT\) benchmark package is now fully reduced.

The mixed overlap family is
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
\]
so the diagonal constant is exactly
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
\]

The derivative vectors are also exact:
\[
\ell_{\bullet}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{\bullet}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{\bullet}^{OO}
+
\ell_{\bullet}^{EO}.
\]

However, the norm constants and Taylor-remainder constants are only controlled by honest upper bounds:
\[
L_{\bullet}^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_{\bullet}^{EE}
+
\frac12L_{\bullet}^{OO}
+
L_{\bullet}^{EO},
\]
\[
C_{\bullet}^{TT}
\le
\frac12C_{\bullet}^{EE}
+
\frac12C_{\bullet}^{OO}
+
C_{\bullet}^{EO}.
\]

Thus the canonical seven-constant package
\[
(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},L_+^{TT},L_-^{TT},L_0^{TT},C_+^{TT},C_-^{TT},C_m^{TT})
\]
is no longer an independent unknown set.

It is a finite assembled package built from the already separated \(EE/OO/EO\) data.

Therefore the mixed same-shell sufficient support condition is fixed as
\[
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
\]

So Audit A is structurally closed.

The next nonredundant step is Audit B:
first compute the principal transverse source from \(TD+DT\),
and only afterwards add the residual correction from \(OD+DO+DD\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Audit B: Exact Principal Transverse Pair from the \(TD+DT\) Blocks}

\section{Goal}

At the current stage, the sharp leading transverse audit starts from the mixed block
\[
TD+DT,
\]
not from the full enlarged correction family.
The exact leading-order task is to extract the principal pair
\[
\Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O,
\]
from the projected one-defect first-order Hessian kernel.

\section{1. Canonical projector extraction}

The background-dependent Hessian is expanded blockwise as
\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\cdots,
\]
and the tangent-projected first-order kernel is
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi)
:=
\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
\]

For the transverse mixed source, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:B_TDDT_def}
\end{equation}

The invariant projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:B_projectors}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact leading transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:B_e0o0_exact}
\end{equation}

At the minimal mixed-block level one identifies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:B_Lambda_identification}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit \(TD\) and \(DT\) block form}

For the defect background
\[
P_B=z_Bz_B^\dagger,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\xi P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)\left(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\right).
}
\label{eq:B_dPB}
\end{equation}
Hence every mixed shell-defect transport block contains one explicit factor of \(\theta'(\xi)\).

The \(TD\) block takes the reduced form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
A_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
A_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right),
}
\label{eq:B_VTD}
\end{equation}
and the \(DT\) block similarly takes the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
B_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
B_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right).
}
\label{eq:B_VDT}
\end{equation}

Therefore the combined principal transverse kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
(A_E+B_E)E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
(A_O+B_O)J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right].
}
\label{eq:B_MTDDT_explicit}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E:=A_E+B_E,
\qquad
C_O:=A_O+B_O.
}
\label{eq:B_CECO}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
C_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
C_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:B_MTDDT_C}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Projection to the invariant pair}

Substituting \eqref{eq:B_MTDDT_C} into \eqref{eq:B_projectors}, one obtains
\begin{align}
e_0^{(1)}
&=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}
\Bigl(
\Sigma_a\,
\theta'(\xi)\bigl[
C_E E_{\mu b}\Sigma_b
+
C_O J_{\mu b}\Sigma_b
\bigr]
\Bigr),
\\
o_0^{(1)}
&=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}
\Bigl(
\Sigma_a\,
\theta'(\xi)\bigl[
C_E E_{\mu b}\Sigma_b
+
C_O J_{\mu b}\Sigma_b
\bigr]
\Bigr).
\end{align}

Under the canonical invariant normalization used in the reduced projector formalism,
the \(E\)- and \(J\)-channels decouple and the Pauli trace gives the standard branch-level result
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12\,C_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
}
\label{eq:B_e0_half}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12\,C_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:B_o0_half}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
}
\label{eq:B_Lambda_half}
\end{equation}
at the minimal \(TD+DT\) level.

\paragraph{Honest status.}
Equations \eqref{eq:B_e0o0_exact} and \eqref{eq:B_Lambda_identification} are the exact leading projector formulas.
Equations \eqref{eq:B_e0_half}--\eqref{eq:B_Lambda_half} are the current branch-level reduced realization of that exact audit.

\section{4. Dictionary to the reduced PDE coefficients}

Once \(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) are extracted,
the reduced coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:B_ab_dict}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:B_Itheta}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:B_ab_fromLambda}
\end{equation}

Combining with \eqref{eq:B_Lambda_half},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:B_ab_fromAB}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Placement inside the full mixed-block audit}

Beyond the minimal truncation, the actual transverse point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:B_fullsum}
\end{equation}

But the sharp leading-order execution order is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \(TD+DT\) exactly;
\item define
\[
v_{\rm pr}
:=
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(TD+DT)},\Lambda_O^{(TD+DT)}\bigr);
\]
\item only afterwards add the residual correction
\[
r_{\rm rem}
:=
\Bigl(
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\;
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=v_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem},
}
\label{eq:B_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_{\rm pr}
=
\left(
\frac12(A_E+B_E),\,
\frac12(A_O+B_O)
\right)
}
\label{eq:B_vpr}
\end{equation}
in the current branch-level reduced realization.

\section{6. Strong survival test after the principal pair is computed}

A strong sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\right|
<
\left|\frac12(A_E+B_E)\right|,
}
\label{eq:B_strongE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\right|
<
\left|\frac12(A_O+B_O)\right|.
}
\label{eq:B_strongO}
\end{equation}

A weaker Euclidean sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|r_{\rm rem}\|_2
<
\|v_{\rm pr}\|_2.
}
\label{eq:B_Euclid}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The \(TD+DT\) principal transverse audit is now completely reduced to the finite pair
\[
(A_E+B_E,\ A_O+B_O).
\]
At the current branch level,
\[
\Lambda_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
\]
hence
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
\]

So the next nonredundant microscopic task is no longer structural:
it is the explicit evaluation of the residual correction vector from
\[
OD,\quad DO,\quad DD.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The principal transverse audit is now reduced exactly to the projected mixed block
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
\]
Its leading transverse coefficient point is extracted by
\[
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
\]

At the current branch-level reduced realization,
\[
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(
A_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+A_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr),
\]
\[
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(
B_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+B_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr),
\]
so the principal pair is
\[
\Lambda_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
\]

Therefore
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
\]

Beyond the minimal truncation, the full transverse point is
\[
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]
But the sharp execution order is:
first compute \(TD+DT\),
then add the residual correction from \(OD,DO,DD\).

Thus the next nonredundant task is the explicit computation of
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
\left(
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\;
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\right),
\]
and the survival test
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=v_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem}\neq(0,0).
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Residual Correction Vector from \(OD+DO+DD\): Exact Projector Formulation}

\section{Goal}

The principal transverse source has already been isolated as
\[
TD+DT,
\]
with leading coefficient point
\[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
\]
What remains is the residual correction carried by
\[
OD,\qquad DO,\qquad DD.
\]

The correct task is therefore not to invent a new mechanism, but to write the exact correction vector
\[
r_{\rm rem}
\]
in the same projector language and derive sharp sufficient non-cancellation criteria.

\section{1. Exact blockwise residual coefficients}

For every candidate transverse block
\[
AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\},
\]
define the tangent-projected first-order kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:R_MAB_def}
\end{equation}

The invariant projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:R_projectors}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact residual blockwise coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB}^{\rm inv}],
}
\label{eq:R_eo_AB}
\end{equation}
for \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\).

This is the exact same executable definition already used for the full mixed-block audit.

\section{2. Exact residual correction vector}

Define the residual correction pair by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm rem}
:=
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:R_De}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\rm rem}
:=
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:R_Do}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in vector form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
:=
\bigl(\Delta e_{\rm rem},\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr)
=
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},\,o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:R_rrem}
\end{equation}

This is the exact residual correction vector.

\section{3. Principal-plus-residual split}

The full transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:R_fullsum}
\end{equation}

Define the principal pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm pr}
:=
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr},\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}\bigr)
=
\bigl(
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:R_rpr}
\end{equation}

Then the full transverse point decomposes exactly as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem}.
}
\label{eq:R_split}
\end{equation}

At the current conservative stage one already uses
\[
e_0^{(1)}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)},
\]
so the same split may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\rm mix},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\rm mix},
}
\label{eq:R_Ksplit}
\end{equation}
with the understanding that the residual part is precisely the \(OD+DO+DD\) completion of the mixed-block correction family.

\section{4. Strong sufficient survival criteria}

A strong componentwise sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\rm rem}|<|\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm rem}|<|\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}|.
}
\label{eq:R_strong_pr}
\end{equation}
Under this condition, the residual blocks cannot kill the principal transverse witness pair componentwise.

At the conservative \(K\)-sector stage this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\rm mix}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm mix}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:R_strong_K}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the already-stated strong sufficient survival condition.

\section{5. Euclidean sufficient survival criterion}

The componentwise condition is strong but not necessary.
A weaker rotationally invariant sufficient criterion follows from the triangle inequality.

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|r_{\rm rem}\|_2<\|r_{\rm pr}\|_2,
}
\label{eq:R_Euclid_pr}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem}\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:R_nonzero_Euclid}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:R_nonzero_pair}
\end{equation}

Indeed,
\[
\|r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem}\|_2
\ge
\bigl|\|r_{\rm pr}\|_2-\|r_{\rm rem}\|_2\bigr|
>0.
\]

Thus the Euclidean criterion is a sharp and basis-independent sufficient test for survival of the transverse pair.

\section{6. Norm bounds in terms of blockwise budgets}

Define the blockwise magnitudes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{AB}
:=
\sqrt{
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr)^2+
\bigl(o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr)^2
},
\qquad
AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}.
}
\label{eq:R_rhoAB}
\end{equation}

Then by the triangle inequality,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|r_{\rm rem}\|_2
\le
\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DO}+\rho_{DD}.
}
\label{eq:R_rrem_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore a practical sufficient condition for transverse survival is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DO}+\rho_{DD}
<
\|r_{\rm pr}\|_2.
}
\label{eq:R_practical_survival}
\end{equation}

This reduces the correction audit to three finite blockwise magnitude estimates.

\section{7. Dictionary to the reduced PDE coefficients}

Once the full transverse point is known,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:R_ab_dict}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:R_ab_final}
\end{equation}

Combining with \eqref{eq:R_split},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:R_alpha_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:R_beta_split}
\end{equation}

In the conservative \(K\)-sector notation this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\rm mix}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\rm mix}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:R_alpha_beta_K}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest conclusion}

What is now fully closed is the exact residual correction formalism:
\begin{enumerate}
\item blockwise exact definitions of \(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\) for \(AB=OD,DO,DD\);
\item the exact residual vector \(r_{\rm rem}\);
\item the exact principal-plus-residual split
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem};
\]
\item strong and Euclidean sufficient survival conditions.
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet inserted numerically is the explicit microscopic evaluation of
\[
\mathcal M_{OD}^{\rm inv},
\qquad
\mathcal M_{DO}^{\rm inv},
\qquad
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\rm inv}.
\]

So the project is now reduced to three literal blockwise projector computations.

\section{Final Summary}

The residual transverse correction is now fully reduced to the three blockwise projector computations
\[
OD,\qquad DO,\qquad DD.
\]

For each residual block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), define
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB}^{\rm inv}].
\]
Then the exact residual correction vector is
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
\bigl(\Delta e_{\rm rem},\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr)
=
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
\]

The full transverse coefficient point splits exactly as
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem},
\]
where \(r_{\rm pr}\) is the already isolated principal \(TD+DT\) source.

Hence the strong componentwise sufficient survival condition is
\[
|\Delta e_{\rm rem}|<|\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm rem}|<|\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}|.
\]
A weaker Euclidean sufficient condition is
\[
\|r_{\rm rem}\|_2<\|r_{\rm pr}\|_2.
\]

Finally, the reduced PDE coefficients are
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr).
\]

Thus the project is now reduced to three literal residual block computations:
\[
\mathcal M_{OD}^{\rm inv},
\qquad
\mathcal M_{DO}^{\rm inv},
\qquad
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\rm inv}.
\]
No further structural theorem is needed.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Residual-Block Closure by Parity Audit: \(OD,DO,DD\)}

\section{Short explanation}

At the current stage, the honest status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD+DT \text{ are the proven leading transverse source blocks,}
}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OD,\ DO,\ DD \text{ are candidate residual corrections beyond the minimal truncation.}
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the correct next step is not to assert that \(OD,DO,DD\) vanish identically,
but to derive a sharp \emph{selection-rule audit} telling us exactly when they vanish and when they must be computed.

\section{1. Exact residual-block definitions}

For each residual block
\[
AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\},
\]
define the tangent-projected first-order kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi)
:=
\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:residual_MAB_def}
\end{equation}

The executable projector formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
}
\label{eq:residual_eo_def}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
}
\label{eq:residual_projectors}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact residual correction vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
\bigl(\Delta e_{\rm rem},\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr)
=
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:residual_vector}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Reflection-parity selection rule}

For a reflection-symmetric defect background, the low modes satisfy
\[
u_a^+(-\xi)=+u_a^+(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(-\xi)=-u_a^-(\xi),
\]
and the projected mixed symbol is
\[
(M^\mu_{AB})_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger(\xi)\,
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,
u_b^-(\xi).
\]

Now the integrand parity is determined entirely by the parity of \(\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}\):

\begin{itemize}
\item if
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi),
\]
then
\[
(u_a^+)^\dagger \mathcal M^\mu_{AB} u_b^-
\]
is odd and integrates to zero;

\item if
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(-\xi)=-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi),
\]
then
\[
(u_a^+)^\dagger \mathcal M^\mu_{AB} u_b^-
\]
is even and can survive.
\end{itemize}

Therefore:

\begin{lemma}[Residual parity-vanishing criterion]
For any block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), if the projected first-order kernel is reflection-even,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:even_kernel_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0.
}
\label{eq:even_kernel_zero}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Because \(u^+\) is even and \(u^-\) is odd, an even kernel produces an odd integrand,
hence every mixed matrix element vanishes.
The projector contractions \(\mathfrak P_E,\mathfrak P_O\) are linear in those matrix elements,
so both coefficients vanish.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Residual survival criterion]
If instead
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)=-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:odd_kernel_condition}
\end{equation}
then the block is parity-allowed to contribute:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)},\ o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\text{ need not vanish and must be computed explicitly.}
}
\label{eq:odd_kernel_survive}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\section{3. Why \(TD+DT\) are leading while \(OD,DO,DD\) are residual}

The reason the sharp current audit starts from \(TD+DT\) is structural:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse source is generated by blocks mixing shell-gradient/current data with defect/projector/tangent data;
\item the explicit current Class II source splits into a transverse part and a primitive longitudinal part;
\item the leading transverse kernel is therefore assigned to \(TD+DT\);
\item \(OD,DO,DD\) are allowed as corrections, but not yet established as leading.
\end{enumerate}

So the correct hierarchy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD+DT \text{ first,}
\qquad
OD+DO+DD \text{ second.}
}
\label{eq:hierarchy_blocks}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Blockwise audit logic for \(OD\) and \(DO\)}

The \(OD\)-type sector has already been reduced in earlier work to an explicit projected self-energy derivative test.
In particular, under \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry one obtains a \(2\times2\) reduced subsector
\[
M_Z^{OD}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO} & (M_Z^{OD})_{OD}\\
(M_Z^{OD})_{DO} & (M_Z^{OD})_{DD}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with the exchange-symmetric reduction
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}.
\]

Then the physical traceless mode is controlled by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
}
\label{eq:OD_phys_lambda}
\end{equation}

This is not yet the same thing as the final transverse pair
\((e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)})\),
but it tells us the honest current status:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OD/DO \text{ are not theorem-level zero.}
}
\label{eq:ODDO_not_zero}
\end{equation}

What is closed is only that their effect has been reduced to an explicit projected contraction/sign test.

\section{5. Blockwise audit logic for \(DD\)}

The present block assignment states that
\[
DD
\]
can
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{renormalize or directly support the final }Q_B\text{-endomorphism-valued doublet structure after Schur reduction.}
}
\label{eq:DD_role}
\end{equation}

Therefore the honest statement is again:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DD \text{ is not proved to vanish identically.}
}
\label{eq:DD_not_zero}
\end{equation}

However, by the parity criterion above, \(DD\) vanishes automatically if its projected first-order kernel is reflection-even:
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
\Longrightarrow
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}=o_{0;DD}^{(1)}=0.
\]

So the \(DD\)-audit is reduced to one binary question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{is }\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}\text{ even or odd under }\xi\mapsto-\xi?
}
\label{eq:DD_binary}
\]

\section{6. Exact residual classification table}

The sharp blockwise status is therefore

\[
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{block} & \text{current theorem-level status} & \text{next exact test} \\
\hline
OD & \text{candidate correction, not proved zero} &
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)\stackrel{?}{=}\pm \mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
\\[2mm]
DO & \text{candidate correction, not proved zero} &
\mathcal M^\mu_{DO,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)\stackrel{?}{=}\pm \mathcal M^\mu_{DO,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
\\[2mm]
DD & \text{candidate correction, not proved zero} &
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)\stackrel{?}{=}\pm \mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
\end{array}
}
\label{eq:residual_status_table}
\]

If the answer is \(+\) for a given block, its contribution vanishes exactly.
If the answer is \(-\), its contribution is parity-allowed and must be computed.

\section{7. Final residual closure statement}

Hence the final residual correction vector splits as follows.

\paragraph{Case I: full even residual sector.}
If all three residual kernels are reflection-even,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{inv}},
\ \mathcal M^\mu_{DO,\mathrm{inv}},
\ \mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
\ \text{are all even},
}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}=0.
}
\label{eq:full_even_case}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case II: partial even/odd mixture.}
If only some are even, then only those vanish.
The remaining odd blocks form the true residual correction:
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
\sum_{\substack{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\\ \mathcal M_{AB}\ \text{odd}}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
\]

\paragraph{Case III: no parity cancellation.}
If all three are odd, then no residual block is killed by parity and the full
\[
OD+DO+DD
\]
projector computation is required.

\section{8. Dictionary to the final reduced coefficients}

The final transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem},
}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\bigr),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

So the final microscopic closure question for the transverse sector has now been reduced to a parity audit followed, only if needed, by literal blockwise projection.

\section{Final Summary}

The residual mixed blocks \(OD,DO,DD\) are not theorem-level zero at the current stage.
They are candidate corrections beyond the proven leading \(TD+DT\) transverse source.

However, there is now an exact parity-based vanishing criterion.

For any residual block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), if
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi),
\]
then
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}=o_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0.
\]

If instead
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)=-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi),
\]
then the block is parity-allowed to contribute and must be computed explicitly.

Thus the residual transverse closure is reduced to a three-block parity audit:
\[
OD,\qquad DO,\qquad DD.
\]

If all three projected kernels are even, then
\[
r_{\rm rem}=0.
\]
Otherwise, only the parity-odd subset survives and contributes to
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem}.
\]

Therefore the final transverse microscopic closure is no longer a structural problem.
It is a literal blockwise parity classification followed, if needed, by explicit projector evaluation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Residual-Block Audit I: Honest Status of the \(OD\) Block}

\section{Goal}

The immediate question is whether the residual correction block
\[
OD
\]
is automatically killed by the already-closed parity/oddness selection rule,
or whether it remains a genuine explicit computation.

\section{1. Why the previously closed oddness theorem does \emph{not} automatically kill \(OD\)}

The already-closed parity fact for the Class-II working branch states that
first-order transport contributions extracted from the linearized
\[
J^{(1)},\qquad K^{(1)}
\]
sector are automatically odd in \(\xi\), because the defect-background gradient enters through
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi).
\]
Therefore the corresponding first-order transport source belongs to the odd transport sector.

However, the \(OD\)-mixed block is not introduced in the current notes as a direct
\(J^{(1)}/K^{(1)}\) transport source.
Instead, it is generated from the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
on the background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
\]

Expanding this interaction gives the background-generated cubic vertices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
}
\label{eq:OD_vertices_closed}
\end{equation}

These vertices then feed the projected bubble self-energies
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\qquad
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min}),
\label{eq:OD_selfenergies_closed}
\end{equation}
rather than the already-isolated direct odd transport source.

Therefore the existing oddness theorem for the direct transport sector does not,
by itself, imply
\[
OD=0.
\]

\section{2. Exact current meaning of the \(OD\) contribution}

The notes reduce the \(OD\)-mixed piece to the explicit kinetic-flow matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:OD_sign_test_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence the \(OD\)-block is already known to be a genuine projected self-energy derivative test.
Its sign is not yet theorem-level fixed by the currently available truncation.

So the honest statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OD \text{ is not proved to vanish identically.}
}
\label{eq:OD_not_zero_theorem}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exchange-symmetric reduction}

If the projected background and regulator preserve
\[
O\leftrightarrow D
\]
exchange symmetry, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO}.
}
\label{eq:OD_exchange}
\end{equation}

In that case the physical traceless mode is controlled by the single eigenvalue
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}.
}
\label{eq:OD_phys_single}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire \(OD\)-mixed bottleneck reduces to one explicit inequality:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0
}
\label{eq:OD_one_ineq}
\end{equation}
if one wants the \(OD\) sector to be isotropizing rather than destabilizing.

\section{4. Consequence for the residual transverse audit}

Because \(OD\) is not killed automatically by the already-closed odd transport theorem,
the correction pair
\[
\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
\]
must be regarded as parity-allowed unless one performs an additional block-specific parity computation
for the actual projected kernel.

Hence the current honest classification is:
\[
\boxed{
OD \text{ is a candidate residual correction that must be explicitly computed.}
}
\]

In particular, one must \emph{not} replace it by zero merely by citing the direct
\(\theta'(\xi)\)-oddness of the \(J/K\)-generated first-order transport source.

\section{5. What is actually closed now}

The strongest closed statement is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the already-proved direct odd transport source controls the leading \(TD+DT\) audit;
\item the \(OD\)-mixed block is structurally different, because it is generated through
background-dependent cubic vertices and projected bubble self-energies;
\item its sign and magnitude are reduced to the explicit projected contraction
\eqref{eq:OD_sign_test_exact};
\item under \(O\leftrightarrow D\) symmetry, the full \(OD\)-question reduces to the single inequality
\eqref{eq:OD_one_ineq}.
\end{enumerate}

Thus \(OD\) is not conceptually open any more, but it is still computationally open.

\section{Final Summary}

The \(OD\)-block is not automatically killed by the already-closed direct odd transport theorem.

That theorem applies to the direct first-order transport source generated from the
background-gradient structure
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
inside the \(J/K\)-based transport sector.

By contrast, the \(OD\)-mixed block arises from the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D,
\]
which generates the background-dependent cubic vertices
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B(\xi),
\]
and therefore feeds a projected bubble self-energy derivative test.

Hence the honest exact current statement is
\[
\boxed{
OD \text{ is not theorem-level zero.}
}
\]

Its contribution is reduced to the explicit projected contraction
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{IJ}
=
-\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial \delta_J}
\frac{\partial}{\partial p^2}
\Sigma_I^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\right|_{p=0,\delta=0},
\qquad
I,J\in\{O,D\}.
\]

If \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry holds, the problem reduces further to the single inequality
\[
\lambda_{OD}^{\mathrm{phys}}
=
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}-(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}<0.
\]

Therefore the \(OD\)-block is a genuine residual correction that must be explicitly computed, not discarded by automatic parity cancellation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Residual-Block Audit II: Honest Status of the \(DO\) Block}

\section{Goal}

After the \(OD\)-audit, the next question is whether the residual block
\[
DO
\]
is automatically killed, or whether it is simply the exchange partner of \(OD\) and therefore remains an explicit projected correction.

\section{1. \(DO\) is already part of the exact mixed-block audit}

The exact transverse candidate family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
}
\label{eq:DO_candidate_family}
\end{equation}
The practical audit order is explicitly fixed as
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
\]
Therefore \(DO\) is not a block that has been removed by a theorem-level symmetry argument.
It is already built into the exact mixed-block audit architecture.

Hence the honest starting point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DO \text{ is a candidate residual correction block.}
}
\label{eq:DO_candidate_status}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Why the direct odd-transport theorem does not automatically kill \(DO\)}

The already-closed direct oddness theorem applies to the explicit first-order transport source generated through the defect-gradient structures
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
in the direct \(J/K\)-generated transport sector.

But \(DO\) is not introduced in the current audit as a direct isolated \(\theta'(\xi)\)-transport source.
It belongs to the same mixed residual family as \(OD\), namely the correction blocks beyond the proven leading source \(TD+DT\).

Therefore the previously closed direct oddness theorem does not, by itself, imply
\[
DO=0.
\]

\section{3. Exchange symmetry with \(OD\)}

In the symmetry-reduced mixed \(OD\) analysis, the projected flow matrix satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_Z^{OD})_{OO}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DD},
\qquad
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO},
}
\label{eq:DO_exchange_equal}
\end{equation}
under \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry.

This has a direct consequence:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{if the projected background and regulator preserve }O\leftrightarrow D,
\text{ then }DO\text{ is not independent of }OD.
}
\label{eq:DO_not_indep}
\end{equation}

In that case, the \(DO\)-block is the exchange partner of the \(OD\)-block,
and both are controlled by the same reduced projected test.

Thus the honest theorem-level statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DO \text{ is not proved to vanish identically,}
}
\label{eq:DO_not_zero}
\end{equation}
but rather
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DO \text{ is exchange-equivalent to }OD
\text{ whenever }O\leftrightarrow D\text{ symmetry holds.}
}
\label{eq:DO_exchange_equiv}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Consequence for the residual transverse pair}

Therefore the correction pair
\[
\bigl(e_{0;DO}^{(1)},o_{0;DO}^{(1)}\bigr)
\]
must be treated as parity-allowed unless one performs either:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a separate blockwise parity computation for \(\mathcal M^\mu_{DO,\mathrm{inv}}\), or
\item an exchange-symmetry reduction identifying it with the corresponding \(OD\) contribution.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the strongest honest current classification is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DO \text{ is a genuine residual correction block that must be explicitly accounted for.}
}
\label{eq:DO_final_classification}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Most economical reduction under exchange symmetry}

If the \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry is exact in the projected mixed sector,
then one may reduce the residual pair by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:DO_equals_OD}
\end{equation}
at the symmetry-reduced level.

Then the residual vector becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DO_OD_reduced_rrem}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest reduction available without overclaiming blockwise vanishing.

\section{Conclusion}

The correct conclusion is not that \(DO\) vanishes.
The correct conclusion is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(DO\) remains inside the exact residual mixed-block audit;
\item the direct odd-transport theorem does not eliminate it automatically;
\item under \(O\leftrightarrow D\) symmetry, it is exchange-equivalent to \(OD\);
\item otherwise it must be computed separately.
\end{enumerate}

So \(DO\) is computationally open but structurally reduced.

\section{Final Summary}

The \(DO\)-block is not theorem-level zero.

It is already part of the exact mixed-block transverse audit:
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
\]
Therefore it cannot be discarded automatically.

Moreover, the already-closed direct odd transport theorem does not eliminate \(DO\),
because that theorem applies to the direct \(J/K\)-generated first-order transport source,
whereas \(DO\) belongs to the residual mixed-block correction family.

If the projected mixed sector preserves \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, then
\[
(M_Z^{OD})_{OD}=(M_Z^{OD})_{DO},
\]
so \(DO\) is exchange-equivalent to \(OD\).
In that symmetry-reduced case one may write
\[
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\]
and therefore
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr).
\]

Thus the honest current status is:
\[
\boxed{
DO \text{ is a genuine residual correction block,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
under }O\leftrightarrow D\text{ symmetry, it is not independent of }OD.
\]

So the next irreducible task is the \(DD\)-audit.

\section{Residual-Block Audit III: Honest Final Status of the \(DD\) Block}

\section{Goal}

The final residual question is whether the block
\[
DD
\]
is automatically absent, or whether it remains a genuine transverse correction even after all currently closed reductions.

\section{1. \(DD\) survives every current reduction layer}

Across the currently available notes, there is a mild drift in how aggressively the residual mixed-block audit is compressed.

In the broad mixed-block audit, the candidate transverse family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
}
\label{eq:DD_broad_family}
\end{equation}

But in the conservative near-final full-Hessian snapshot, the remaining unresolved blocks are reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TT,\ TD,\ DT,\ DD.
}
\label{eq:DD_conservative_family}
\end{equation}

This is an important consistency fact:
even when the audit is compressed conservatively, the \(DD\)-block still survives.

Therefore the honest theorem-level statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DD \text{ is not a dispensable block in the present microscopic program.}
}
\label{eq:DD_not_disp}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Why \(DD\) is structurally different from \(OD\) and \(DO\)}

The \(DD\)-block acts entirely inside the defect-tangent doublet sector.
Hence, after tangent projection,
it directly defines a \(Q_B\)-endomorphism-valued first-order kernel.

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:DD_generic_kernel}
\end{equation}

Therefore the executable projector formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}),
}
\label{eq:DD_e_projector}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}).
}
\label{eq:DD_o_projector}
\end{equation}

So \(DD\) is not merely an exchange partner of some other block.
It carries its own direct transverse projection channels.

\section{3. Honest physical role of the \(DD\)-block}

The current notes already isolate the two structurally allowed roles of \(DD\):

\begin{enumerate}
\item direct support of the transverse doublet;
\item renormalization of the already-induced \(TD/DT\) transport.
\end{enumerate}

This means that the correct current statement is not
\[
DD=0,
\]
but rather
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DD \text{ is a genuine transverse candidate,}
}
\label{eq:DD_genuine_candidate}
\end{equation}
with the additional structural expectation that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DD \text{ is more likely to renormalize the mixed-shell carrier than to generate it from nothing.}
}
\label{eq:DD_renorm_expectation}
\end{equation}

The second statement is an honest structural expectation from the present notes,
not yet a theorem of vanishing or dominance.

\section{4. Why there is no automatic parity-killing theorem for \(DD\) at present}

A parity-killing theorem would require a closed proof that
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
\]
on the actual projected one-defect background.

But the current background-dependent Hessian library does not provide such a theorem.
Instead, the \(DD\)-sector contains
\[
\mathcal H_{DD}
=
-Z_{D,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{DD}(\xi,\partial_y),
\]
so the actual first-order kernel inherits contributions from:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect-background-dependent potential tensor,
\item derivative-anisotropy terms,
\item the explicit first-order transport operator \(\mathcal T_{DD}\).
\end{enumerate}

Hence the parity of \(\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}\) is not theorem-level fixed by the current notes.

Therefore the strongest honest statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
DD \text{ is not proved to vanish by parity.}
}
\label{eq:DD_not_parity_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Exact place of \(DD\) inside the final transverse pair}

The exact full transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:DD_full_pair}
\end{equation}

In the sharper conservative reduction, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:DD_conservative_e}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_0^{(1)}
=
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:DD_conservative_o}
\end{equation}

So among all residual blocks, \(DD\) is the one that persists even in the conservative compression of the audit.

\section{6. Strongest honest \(DD\)-classification}

Combining all currently closed facts, the sharp classification is:

\[
\boxed{
DD \text{ is not theorem-level zero,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
DD \text{ has direct projector-visible transverse channels }(E,O),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
DD \text{ survives even the conservative reduced audit,}
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
DD \text{ must be explicitly computed unless a new block-specific parity theorem is proved.}
}
\]

\section{7. Final closure statement for the residual sector}

The residual sector is now sharply separated into two layers.

\paragraph{Exchange-type residuals.}
The blocks \(OD\) and \(DO\) are residual mixed blocks, and under
\(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry they are not independent.

\paragraph{Intrinsic defect-tangent residual.}
The block \(DD\) is different:
it acts intrinsically inside the defect-tangent doublet sector and couples directly to the transverse projectors.

Thus the final residual correction vector can be written schematically as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
r_{OD/DO}
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:DD_rrem_split}
\end{equation}
where \(r_{OD/DO}\) may simplify under exchange symmetry, but the \(DD\)-piece remains genuinely intrinsic.

\section{Conclusion}

The correct final conclusion is not that \(DD\) vanishes.
The correct final conclusion is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(DD\) remains present in both the broad and conservative residual audits;
\item \(DD\) has direct transverse projector channels through \(a_{E;DD}\) and \(a_{O;DD}\);
\item no theorem-level parity cancellation is currently available for \(DD\);
\item therefore \(DD\) is the final unavoidable explicit residual projector computation.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The \(DD\)-block is the final intrinsically surviving residual block.

It remains present in both the broad mixed-block audit
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD,
\]
and in the conservative reduced audit
\[
TT,\ TD,\ DT,\ DD.
\]

Moreover, the projected \(DD\)-kernel already has the explicit transverse decomposition
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
so the corresponding coefficients
\[
e_{0;DD}^{(1)},\qquad o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
\]
are direct projector-visible transverse candidates.

Therefore the honest theorem-level conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
DD \text{ is not automatically zero,}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
DD \text{ must be explicitly computed unless a new block-specific parity theorem is established.}
}
\]

Structurally, the sharp current expectation is that \(DD\) is more likely to renormalize the
already-induced \(TD/DT\) transverse carrier than to generate it from nothing,
but this is not yet a theorem of vanishing or dominance.

So the residual sector is now fully classified:
\(OD\) and \(DO\) are exchange-type residual corrections,
while \(DD\) is the final intrinsic defect-tangent residual block.

\mathcal D_{\rm can}(p)
=
\rho_1\otimes A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{\rm can}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1-p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
\alpha(p_1+p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{\rm can}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
v_\perp^{\rm can}q_1\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
v_\perp^{\rm can}q_2\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
}
\]

\section{Completed Canonical Mixed-Branch PDE}

For the canonical mixed odd-active branch
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\]
the exact mixed-branch master symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

Therefore the coefficient sheet is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Hence
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha\Big[(p_1-p_2)\sigma_1+(p_1+p_2)\sigma_2\Big].
\]

Equivalently, introducing rotated transverse momenta
\[
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2},
\]
one obtains
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
v_\perp^{\rm can}(q_1\sigma_1+q_2\sigma_2),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\rm can}
=
\sqrt2\,\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt6\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Therefore the completed reduced PDE on the current working branch is
\[
\boxed{
\Big[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\rm can}\,
\big(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\big)
\Big]\chi=0.
}
\]

The corresponding dispersion relation is
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(v_\perp^{\rm can})^2(q_1^2+q_2^2)
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{128}\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

The anisotropy ratio is
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{\rm can}
=
\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{v_\perp^{\rm can}}
=
\frac{3}{32\sqrt2}\,
\frac{\alpha_XL_*}{\beta_X}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

The canonical mixed-branch same-shell acceptance condition is
\[
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\]

Finally, the most complete correction-dressed microscopic target remains
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
}
\]

\section{Finite-Scalar-Upgraded Working PDE}

\section{Short explanation}

The reduced Dirac-type PDE is already closed at branch level.
To go one step further, the correct move is to replace the abstract coefficient triplet
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
by the finite scalar packages that are already isolated in the notes.

At the current honest stage, this gives the strongest currently justified microscopic PDE:
a branch-consistent reduced Dirac PDE whose coefficients are explicitly expressed in terms of the finite scalar audits
\[
\mathcal N_{JJ},\quad m_\parallel,\quad u_\parallel,\quad A_{G_*},
\qquad
\mathfrak T_E,\quad \mathfrak T_O.
\]

\section{1. Exact overlap dictionary}

The exact local overlap dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\lambda_c,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:fs_dict}
\end{equation}
Using the explicit defect overlaps,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:fs_overlaps}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:fs_lambda_general}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:fs_alpha_beta_general}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Longitudinal finite scalar reduction}

At the current working branch level, the longitudinal source is reduced to the \(JJ\)-type finite scalar package:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:fs_lambdacJJ}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal coefficient becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\sim
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|\,A_{G_*}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:fs_lambdaJJ}
\end{equation}

Here the symbol \(\sim\) means:
this is the current finite-scalar working-branch reduction,
not yet the unconditional final exact coefficient of complete TECT.

\paragraph{Executable subformulas.}
The shell-normal asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr)
=
\frac12\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:fs_upar}
\end{equation}
The shell asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:fs_Delta00}
\end{equation}
The longitudinal geometric scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:fs_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at the branch-level notation used earlier,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_X L_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:fs_lambdaLstar}
\end{equation}
where \(L_*\) is the finite longitudinal matrix element extracted from the shell-normal projected \(J\)-sector.

\section{3. Transverse finite scalar reduction}

The transverse source is reduced to the finite scalar contractions
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_O.
}
\label{eq:fs_LambdaEO}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
\sim
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak T_E\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:fs_alphaTE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
\sim
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak T_O\,
\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:fs_betaTO}
\end{equation}

Again, \(\mathfrak T_E,\mathfrak T_O\) are the remaining branch-specific finite scalar contractions of the principal mixed \(JK+KJ\) source and its completion.

\section{4. Finite-scalar-upgraded reduced PDE}

The reduced \(2\times2\) symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:fs_symbol}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:fs_lambdaJJ}, \eqref{eq:fs_alphaTE}, \eqref{eq:fs_betaTO}, the strongest currently justified microscopic PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigg[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigg]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:fs_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
\sim
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|A_{G_*}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:fs_vpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_E
\sim
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak T_E\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:fs_vE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_O
\sim
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak T_O\,
\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:fs_vO}
\end{equation}

This is the finite-scalar-upgraded working PDE.

\section{5. Dispersion relation}

Squaring the reduced symbol gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(v_E^2+v_O^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:fs_disp}
\end{equation}

So the transverse speed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp
=
\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}
\sim
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\,
\sqrt{\mathfrak T_E^2+\mathfrak T_O^2}\,
|\theta_0\kappa|.
}
\label{eq:fs_vperp}
\end{equation}

The exact anisotropy ratio is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\rm fs}
:=
\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}
\sim
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,|G_*|A_{G_*}
}{
\sqrt{\mathfrak T_E^2+\mathfrak T_O^2}
}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:fs_rho}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact finite nondegeneracy criterion}

The reduced Dirac phase is nondegenerate if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:fs_nondeg_exact}
\end{equation}
At the finite-scalar working level this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,|G_*|A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\mathfrak T_E,\mathfrak T_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:fs_nondeg_scalars}
\end{equation}

So the PDE is fully populated up to a finite scalar audit, not an unknown functional derivation.

\section{7. Support-side condition}

The same-shell support side remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:fs_support}
\end{equation}

Therefore the honest final acceptance statement for the current working PDE is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{finite-scalar nondegeneracy}
\quad+\quad
\text{same-shell support}
\quad+\quad
\text{remote-gap support}.
}
\label{eq:fs_acceptance}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The branch-level reduced PDE can be pushed one step further to a finite-scalar-upgraded working PDE.

The exact overlap dictionary is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\lambda_c,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
with
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad

=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

At the current finite-scalar working level,

\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|A_{G_*},
\]
and
\[
\Lambda_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_O.
\]

Therefore the strongest currently justified microscopic PDE is
\[
\Big[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2))
-

\Big]\chi=0,
\]
with
\[
v_\parallel
\sim
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,

m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|A_{G_*}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[

\sim
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,

Its dispersion is
