\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_2
:=
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A|-|R_N|>0,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:G2}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Gate 3: transverse support}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{3,\mathrm{tr}}
:=
|c_E|+|c_O|>0,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_{3,\mathrm{cal}}
:=
|C_E|+|C_O|>0.
}
\label{eq:G3}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Gate 4: constant-sector protection}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}\wedge\text{Gate 2}\wedge\text{Gate 3}\wedge\text{Gate 4}
\Longrightarrow
\text{actual branch-level protected anisotropic massless Dirac carrier.}
}
\label{eq:certificate_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. One-defect acceptance form}

At the one-defect level, the decisive inequalities reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c,
}
\label{eq:onedefect_pass}
\end{equation}
with
\[
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad

\]
The exact longitudinal burden ratio is

\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_final}
\end{equation}

So the one-defect problem is also reduced to the same finite scalar insertion layer.

The remaining frontier is no longer a missing PDE architecture.
It is the explicit evaluation of the finite scalar set

\section{Final Summary}

Yes: for the intended Class II / canonical working branch, the actual microscopic carrier PDE is now reduced to a finite scalar audit.

\section{Explicit Canonical Finite Audit and the Fully Inserted One-Defect Pass Sheet}

\section{The \texorpdfstring{$\mu_\infty$}{mu∞}-First Audit in Fully Executable Form}

\section{Short explanation}

\[

At the current stage this is no longer a conceptual issue.
It is a literal finite constitutive sign test.

\section{1. Exact asymptotic constitutive scalar}

The asymptotic bulk mass parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.

\label{eq:muinf_exec}

\begin{equation}

:=

\label{eq:Delta_mu_exec}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}

}
\label{eq:muinf_Deltamu}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact sign reduction}

Assume the standard normalization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:z0_positive_exec}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta_\mu.
}
\label{eq:muinf_sign_exec}
\end{equation}

Therefore exactly one of the following holds:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu>0
\iff
\mu_\infty>0,
}
\label{eq:mu_pass}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu=0
\iff
\mu_\infty=0,
}
\label{eq:mu_gapless}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu<0
\iff
\mu_\infty<0.
}
\label{eq:mu_reject}
\end{equation}

So the bulk gate is completely executable:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }\Delta_\mu
\text{ and check its sign.}
}
\label{eq:mu_exec_rule}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Simplest vacuum branch}

If the asymptotic branch is vacuum-like,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_\infty=0,

\label{eq:mu_vacuum_exec}

\begin{equation}

\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_vacuum_sign_exec}
\end{equation}

Thus on the simplest vacuum branch the entire bulk audit collapses to a single scalar sign.

\section{4. Non-vacuum asymptotic branch}

\label{eq:mu_nonvac_exec}

\end{equation}
which is weaker than demanding \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\).

\paragraph{Case C: sign-indefinite asymptotic sector.}

=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\bigr).

\end{equation}

\section{5. Earliest reject theorem}

Under \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\), if

\end{equation}
so the branch is rejected before any insertion of
\[

Thus the correct finite audit order really is

\;\longrightarrow\;
g_E
\;\longrightarrow\;
g_c
\;\longrightarrow\;

\;\longrightarrow\;

\end{equation}

\boxed{
\chi_\infty
=
\frac13(2X_{\perp,\infty}+X_{\parallel,\infty})
=
0.
}
\label{eq:vac_chi_zero}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:vac_chi_zero} into \eqref{eq:vac_mu_exact}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:vac_mu_reduced}
\end{equation}

Therefore, under \eqref{eq:vac_z0_pos},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:vac_mu_sign_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Honest consequence}

This is the strongest executable closure of the bulk gate currently available from the notes.

On a generic non-vacuum asymptotic Class-II branch, the sign condition is the balance inequality
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty).
\]
But on the simplest vacuum branch, the asymptotic Class-II correction disappears identically,
so the bulk gate is no longer a balance problem.
It is a one-sign problem.

Hence the constitutive bulk gate is closed once the chosen branch satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:vac_constitutive_gate}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Explicit canonical one-defect acceptance sheet after bulk closure}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
the practical lowest-channel acceptance problem had already been reduced to
\[
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:vac_mu_sign_final}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:vac_four_checks_final}
\end{equation}

So the explicit one-defect acceptance theorem on the simplest vacuum branch is reduced to four finite scalar checks.

\section{4. The resulting explicit working PDE}

On the same explicit canonical branch, the transport coefficients are already fixed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:vac_gc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:vac_gE}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit reduced carrier PDE on this asymptotic branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:vac_explicit_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:vac_beta_zero}
\end{equation}

So the branch is now bulk-closed up to the single constitutive sign \(m(\sigma_\infty)\).

\section{5. Honest status after this step}

What is now closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(\mu_\infty\)-gate is reduced to a single scalar sign on the simplest vacuum branch;
\item the explicit one-defect acceptance sheet is reduced to the four checks in \eqref{eq:vac_four_checks_final};
\item the bulk-side frontier is no longer conceptual.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not inserted numerically:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual sign of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\);
\item the sign of \(\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\);
\item the burden ratio \(\xi_c/\xi_E\);
\item the remote-gap margin \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The strongest executable bulk closure is obtained by fixing the asymptotic constitutive branch to the simplest vacuum branch
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0.
\]
Then
\[
\chi_\infty=0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty=\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
\]

Under the standard normalization \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\), the bulk gate becomes
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]

Therefore, for the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
the practical one-defect acceptance problem reduces to the four finite scalar checks
\[
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

So the bulk side is closed on this branch.
What remains is only finite insertion.

\section{Closure of the Longitudinal Burden Gate on the Explicit Canonical Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

After the bulk gate \(\mu_\infty>0\), the next genuine finite audit is the longitudinal burden ratio.
On the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
this gate is no longer structural.
It is a literal finite inequality on the ratio \(\xi_c/\xi_E\).

\section{1. Exact ratio formula}

The dimensionless burden ratio is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c:=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}.
}
\label{eq:Rc_exact_gate}
\end{equation}

On the explicit canonical branch, the extracted coefficients are
\[
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Rc_branch_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact lowest-channel acceptance window}

For the practically most relevant lowest channel
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
the one-defect criterion reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1.
}
\label{eq:Rc_window_exact}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:Rc_branch_explicit}, this is exactly equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\label{eq:xic_xie_window}
\end{equation}

So the burden gate is now a single explicit finite ratio bound.

\section{3. Equivalent transport-dominance form}

The sharp reduced inequality can also be written directly in transport variables as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c.
}
\label{eq:transport_dominance_gc_gE}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using the canonical matrix normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\,\alpha
>
\frac{\xi_c}{C_\parallel}\,\lambda_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:transport_dominance_alpha_lambda}
\end{equation}

Thus the physical meaning of the gate is simple:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the matched transverse splitting must dominate the matched longitudinal burden.}
}
\label{eq:physical_meaning_burden}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Automatic-pass region in the small-defect regime}

From \eqref{eq:xic_xie_window}, the gate is automatically satisfied whenever
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|}\left|\frac{\xi_E}{\xi_c}\right|.
}
\label{eq:small_defect_autopass_sq}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\theta_0\kappa|
<
\sqrt{
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|}\left|\frac{\xi_E}{\xi_c}\right|
}.
}
\label{eq:small_defect_autopass}
\end{equation}

Hence the burden window is naturally broad in the small-defect regime.
Unless \(|\xi_c/\xi_E|\) is abnormally large, the burden gate is not fine-tuned.

\section{5. Explicit benchmark values}

Under the unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=z_{0,0}=1,
\]
the ratio formula becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c=0.09375\,\xi_c\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Rc_unit}
\end{equation}
So the exact window is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\xi_c|<\frac{32}{3(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\label{eq:xi_c_unit_window}
\end{equation}

Representative values are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.1
\Longrightarrow
|\xi_c/\xi_E|<1066.666\ldots
}
\label{eq:xi_window_01}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.3
\Longrightarrow
|\xi_c/\xi_E|<118.518\ldots
}
\label{eq:xi_window_03}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=1
\Longrightarrow
|\xi_c/\xi_E|<10.666\ldots
}
\label{eq:xi_window_1}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Combination with the already-closed bulk gate}

On the simplest vacuum asymptotic branch, the bulk gate has already reduced to
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]
Therefore the explicit canonical one-defect acceptance sheet now becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:four_scalar_sheet_closed}
\end{equation}

So after the \(\mu_\infty\)-closure, the burden gate is also fully executable.

\section{7. Honest status after this step}

What is now closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the bulk gate is reduced to the sign of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\) on the simplest vacuum branch;
\item the longitudinal burden gate is reduced to the explicit ratio window \eqref{eq:xic_xie_window};
\item the physical content of the inequality is the dominance condition \eqref{eq:transport_dominance_alpha_lambda};
\item in the small-defect regime, the burden gate is naturally broad.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not inserted numerically:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual branch value of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\);
\item the actual matched ratio \(\xi_c/\xi_E\);
\item the remote-gap margin \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The longitudinal burden gate is now fully executable on the explicit canonical branch.

Its exact form is
\[
R_c=\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
\]
and in the practically relevant lowest-channel case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,
\]
the exact acceptance window is
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the physical transport meaning is
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c,
}
\]
or in normalized coefficient form
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\alpha>\frac{\xi_c}{C_\parallel}\lambda_\parallel.
}
\]

In the small-defect regime, the window is naturally broad:
\[
|\theta_0\kappa|
<
\sqrt{
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|}\left|\frac{\xi_E}{\xi_c}\right|
}.
\]

Combining this with the already-closed bulk gate on the simplest vacuum branch,
the explicit canonical one-defect acceptance sheet is
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

So the remaining frontier is reduced to finite insertion of branch data.

\section{Explicit Remote-Gap Pass Certificate on the Canonical Explicit Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

At this stage, Gate 1 is no longer a structural theorem problem.
On the explicit canonical branch, it is a single finite scalar margin test.

The exact support condition remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\label{eq:G1_exact_support}
\end{equation}
or, on the explicitly inserted branch notation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_full_support}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Benchmark side}

The exact benchmark side is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:G1_benchmark_master}
\end{equation}

On the explicit canonical branch \(T_\star=T^1,\ \eta=z_0,\ \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0\), the sharpest same-shell usable insertion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
:=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:G1_Xinon}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(0)}\bigr)^2.
}
\label{eq:G1_aK}
\end{equation}

Thus, for the explicit branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:G1_benchmark_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Residual side}

The exact residual decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_residual_split}
\end{equation}

For the explicit branch, the practically inserted upper bound is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_eta_rem_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Signed margin}

Define the actual remote-gap margin
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_margin_def}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:G1_benchmark_explicit} and \eqref{eq:G1_eta_rem_explicit}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_margin_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore Gate 1 passes if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_pass_iff}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Spectral consequence}

If \(\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0\), then the remote block has a uniform positive spectral gap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho),
}
\label{eq:G1_gap_spec}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
=
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)
>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_gap_value}
\end{equation}

So the low shell slot is spectrally isolated once this one scalar margin is positive.

\section{5. Practical two-subproblem reduction}

The same-shell non-enriched benchmark is already reduced to a finite Hermitian eigenvalue problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_j|\lambda_j^{(N)}(p)|,
}
\label{eq:G1_nonenr_eval}
\end{equation}
and the usable entry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:G1_nonenr_usable}
\end{equation}

Hence the real unresolved Gate-1 tasks are exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) one finite same-shell non-enriched eigenvalue computation,}
}
\label{eq:G1_task_i}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) one remote-mixing norm bound } \eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_task_ii}
\end{equation}

Everything else in \(\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)\) is already explicit.

\section{6. Final explicit one-defect acceptance sheet}

Combining the already closed bulk gate and burden gate on the simplest vacuum asymptotic branch, the explicit canonical one-defect pass sheet becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
}
\label{eq:final_four_scalar_sheet_with_gap}
\end{equation}

This is the fully executable practical pass certificate for the explicit canonical branch.

\section{7. Honest status}

What is now closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap gate is reduced to the single scalar margin \(\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)\);
\item the benchmark side is explicit;
\item the residual side is explicit as an upper bound;
\item the one-defect pass sheet is reduced to four scalar checks.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not inserted numerically:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)\), equivalently the same-shell non-enriched finite eigenvalue slot;
\item the residual constants \(C_{\mathrm{high,non}},K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The remote-gap gate is now reduced to a single scalar margin
\[
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
Gate 1 passes if and only if
\[
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
\]

On the explicit canonical branch, the benchmark side is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\},
\]
with
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
\]

The residual side is bounded by
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+

+

+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Therefore the explicit canonical one-defect acceptance sheet is now
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},

\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
\]

So the only genuinely unresolved Gate-1 tasks are:
one same-shell non-enriched finite eigenvalue computation
and one remote-mixing residual bound.

\section{A Sharp Sufficient Positivity Cut for \texorpdfstring{$\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)$}{Xi_non^(1)(rho)}}

\section{Short explanation}

\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho).

At this stage, the correct move is not another structural reduction.
It is to isolate a clean static margin and compare it against the total \(\rho\)-dependent drift budget.

\section{1. Exact starting point}

The explicit canonical-branch benchmark slot is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_non_start}

Define the static core margin
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}
:=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-

Then

\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_non_split}
\end{equation}

So the exact positivity condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}
>
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_exact_pos}
\end{equation}

\section{2. First sharp sufficient condition}

Therefore a first clean sufficient condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_first_suff}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)>0
\quad\Longleftarrow\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_first_suff_equiv}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Explicit drift estimate}

For the minimal same-shell non-enriched block, the small-\(p\) drift satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+ + C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_- + C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B + C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:eps_small_exact}
\end{equation}

At leading order this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
=
\rho\,L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}+O(\rho^2),
\qquad
L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}:=\sqrt{A_+^2+A_-^2+2B^2}.
}
\label{eq:eps_small_leading}
\end{equation}

Introduce any quadratic constant \(C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\rho\,L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}
+
C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}\rho^2.
}
\label{eq:eps_small_quad}
\end{equation}

Now absorb the second remainder into a similar bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\rho\,\widetilde L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}
+
\widetilde C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}\rho^2.
}
\label{eq:eps_nonenr_quad}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\rho\,L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}
+
C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}\rho^2,
}
\label{eq:eps_total_quad}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}
:=
L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}+\widetilde L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)},
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}
:=
C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}+\widetilde C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:LtotCtot}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final explicit sufficient cut}

Substituting \eqref{eq:eps_total_quad} into \eqref{eq:Xi_exact_pos}, one gets the clean sufficient criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho\,L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}
+
C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}\rho^2
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_final_sufficient_cut}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest practical positivity cut in scalar form.

\section{5. Explicit \(\rho\)-window}

If \(C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}>0\), then \eqref{eq:Xi_final_sufficient_cut} is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<\rho<\rho_{\max}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:rho_window_form}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\max}^{(1)}
=
\frac{
-\;L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}
+
\sqrt{
\bigl(L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}\bigr)^2
+
4C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}
}
}{
2C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}
}.
}
\label{eq:rho_max_exact}
\end{equation}

If instead \(C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}=0\), then the sufficient window reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<\rho<
\frac{\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}}{L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}}.
}
\label{eq:rho_max_linear}
\end{equation}

So the same-shell non-enriched positivity gate is completely reduced to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\rho<\rho_{\max}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_two_scalar_cut}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Most transparent static condition}

The static positivity of the slot requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
>
4uA^2+2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}.
}
\label{eq:static_core_condition}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(0)}\bigr)^2,
}
\label{eq:aK_repeat}
\end{equation}
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
>
4uA^2
+
2\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(0)}\bigr)^2
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}.
}
\label{eq:static_core_condition_explicit}
\end{equation}

This is the clean static benchmark-side dominance condition.

\section{7. Final Gate-1 pass certificate}

Hence the explicit canonical branch Gate-1 certificate can be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0
\quad\Longleftarrow\quad
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}-\rho L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}-C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}\rho^2
\Biggr\}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_final_certificate}
\end{equation}

This is the fully executable scalar pass condition.

\section{8. Combination with the already closed branch gates}

Therefore the explicit canonical one-defect acceptance sheet is now
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0,
}
\label{eq:full_four_scalar_sheet}
\end{equation}
and a sufficient concrete version is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}>0,
\qquad
\rho<\rho_{\max}^{(1)},
\qquad
\min\{4K-|r_*|,\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},q_*^2|(\lambda+\mu)+g^2/(M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2)|\}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:fully_concrete_pass_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The same-shell non-enriched benchmark slot is now reduced to a clean scalar positivity cut.

Define
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}
:=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}.
\]
Then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
\]

A sharp practical sufficient condition is
\[
\rho L_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}+C_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}\rho^2
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{core}}^{(1)},
\]
which implies
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)>0.
\]

Hence the Gate-1 margin
\[
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\]
is fully reduced to a scalar comparison problem.

Therefore the explicit canonical one-defect acceptance sheet is now
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},\qquad
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
\]

So the remaining frontier is no longer structural.
It is only finite scalar insertion and comparison.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Practical Final Acceptance Theorem on the Explicit Canonical Branch}

\section{Goal}

We now bundle the previously separated finite scalar checks into a single practical acceptance theorem for the explicit canonical working branch.

The branch is fixed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0.
}
\label{eq:final_branch_choice}
\end{equation}

The exact reduced one-defect lowest-channel acceptance conditions are already known to be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_invariant_sheet}
\end{equation}

We now rewrite these conditions entirely in explicit scalar form.

\section{1. Explicit branch dictionaries}

The burden ratio is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:final_Rc_explicit}
\end{equation}

On the simplest vacuum asymptotic branch
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0,
\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\]
the bulk gate reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:final_mu_explicit}
\end{equation}

The transverse sign condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:final_alpha_sign}
\end{equation}

The remote-gap gate is encoded by the scalar margin
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
}
\label{eq:final_gap_margin}
\end{equation}
and passes iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
}
\label{eq:final_gap_pass}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Final explicit scalar sheet}

Using \eqref{eq:final_Rc_explicit}, the window
\[
-1<R_c<1
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\label{eq:final_ratio_window}
\end{equation}

Therefore the invariant sheet \eqref{eq:final_invariant_sheet} is equivalent to the explicit scalar sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
}
\label{eq:final_explicit_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Witness nondegeneracy}

On the same explicit branch, the carrier coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\Gamma_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,u_\parallel(T^1)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:final_lambda_witness}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:final_alpha_beta_witness}
\end{equation}

Hence a practical sufficient witness nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{JJ}\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1)\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:final_witness_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:final_witness_nonzero},
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha\neq0,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
so the explicit canonical branch is already a nondegenerate carrier witness branch.

\section{4. Practical final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Practical explicit-branch one-defect pass theorem]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0;
\]
\item the lowest projected channel satisfies
\[
|\kappa_*|=1;
\]
\item the asymptotic branch is the simplest vacuum branch,
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0,
\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0;
\]
\item the explicit scalar sheet
\eqref{eq:final_explicit_sheet}
holds;
\item the witness nondegeneracy condition
\eqref{eq:final_witness_nonzero}
holds.
\end{enumerate}
Then the branch passes the practical one-defect one-mode audit and defines an explicit nondegenerate carrier witness branch.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:final_mu_explicit}, the bulk gate is equivalent to \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\).
By \eqref{eq:final_alpha_sign}, the sign condition \(\alpha>0\) is equivalent to \(\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0\).
By \eqref{eq:final_ratio_window}, the lowest-channel window \(-1<R_c<1\) is equivalent to the explicit ratio bound.
By \eqref{eq:final_gap_pass}, the remote-gap support is equivalent to \(\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0\).
Hence \eqref{eq:final_explicit_sheet} is exactly equivalent to the invariant practical acceptance sheet \eqref{eq:final_invariant_sheet}.

Finally, \eqref{eq:final_witness_nonzero} implies
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,\qquad \alpha\neq0,\qquad \beta=0,
\]
so the accepted branch is a nondegenerate explicit carrier witness branch.
\end{proof}

\section{5. Honest status}

This theorem closes the \emph{explicit canonical branch} at the practical one-defect witness level.

It does \emph{not} yet imply that the canonical mixed odd-active branch has been fully populated, because that branch still awaits the two remaining finite microscopic audits:
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},L_\pm^{TT},L_0^{TT},C_\pm^{TT},C_m^{TT},
\qquad
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
\]

So the explicit canonical branch now has a practical final pass theorem,
whereas the mixed odd-active branch still has a finite coefficient-population problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0
\]
now admits a practical final acceptance theorem.

Its invariant one-defect lowest-channel acceptance sheet
\[
-1<R_c<1,\qquad
\alpha>0,\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\]
is exactly equivalent to the explicit scalar sheet
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},\qquad
\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{gap}}(\rho)>0.
\]

If, in addition, the witness nondegeneracy conditions
\[
\Gamma_{JJ}\neq0,\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1)\neq0,\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0
\]
hold, then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
\alpha\neq0,\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
so the branch is a nondegenerate explicit carrier witness branch.

This closes the explicit canonical branch at the practical one-defect witness level.

However, this still does not fully populate the canonical mixed odd-active branch,
which remains two finite microscopic audits away from its final reduced coefficient point.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Conditional Final Acceptance Theorem for the Canonical Mixed Odd-Active Branch}

\section{Goal}

We now state the sharpest honest final theorem currently available for the canonical mixed odd-active branch.

The branch data are fixed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_branch_data}
\end{equation}

The exact reduced mixed-branch coefficient sheet is already fixed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:mixed_branch_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:mixed_branch_ab}
\end{equation}

What remains are exactly two finite microscopic audits.

\section{1. Audit A: mixed same-shell support}

For the canonical mixed branch one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_same_shell_data}
\end{equation}

The exact branch-consistent sufficient same-shell support condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_same_shell_support}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in scalar locked-core form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_same_shell_support_scalar}
\end{equation}

The only not-yet-inserted same-shell constants are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},
\qquad
L_+^{TT},\ L_-^{TT},\ L_0^{TT},
\qquad
C_+^{TT},\ C_-^{TT},\ C_m^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_seven_constants}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Audit B: mixed-block transverse cancellation}

The exact leading transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_eo_sum}
\end{equation}

At the current conservative stage,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\approx0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\approx \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_conservative_stage}
\end{equation}

Define the mixed-block correction pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
:=
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)}+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:mixed_de_mix}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
:=
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:mixed_do_mix}
\end{equation}

Then the actual transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_LambdaEO_actual}
\end{equation}

A strong sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:mixed_strong_survival}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Final populated coefficient point after the two audits}

Once the seven same-shell constants are inserted and
\[
(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}})
\]
are computed, the final mixed-branch microscopic coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:mixed_final_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:mixed_final_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:mixed_final_beta}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_\parallel P_*=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
P_*K_1P_*=\alpha(\sigma_1+\sigma_2),
\qquad
P_*K_2P_*=\alpha(\sigma_2-\sigma_1),
}
\label{eq:mixed_projected_target}
\end{equation}
in the canonical symmetric mixed case \(\alpha=\beta\).

\section{4. Conditional final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional final acceptance theorem for the canonical mixed odd-active branch]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the canonical mixed branch data \eqref{eq:mixed_branch_data};
\item the same-shell support inequality \eqref{eq:mixed_same_shell_support};
\item the strong mixed-block survival condition \eqref{eq:mixed_strong_survival};
\item the longitudinal primitive seed survives, i.e.
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq 0;
\]
\item the constant-sector protection and remote-gap support already closed at working-branch level remain valid.
\end{enumerate}
Then the canonical mixed odd-active branch defines a nondegenerate odd-active reduced microscopic carrier, with final coefficient point
\eqref{eq:mixed_final_lpar}--\eqref{eq:mixed_final_beta}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:mixed_same_shell_support}, the same-shell slot remains spectrally admissible on the canonical mixed branch.
By \eqref{eq:mixed_strong_survival}, the mixed-block corrections cannot cancel the already explicit \(K\)-sector transverse witness pair.
Hence \((\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0)\).
If in addition \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq0\), then \(\lambda_\parallel\neq0\).
Therefore the final reduced microscopic coefficient point is nondegenerate and given by
\eqref{eq:mixed_final_lpar}--\eqref{eq:mixed_final_beta}.
\end{proof}

\section{5. Honest status}

This theorem is the sharpest currently justified endpoint for the canonical mixed odd-active branch.

It says:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{no new structural theorem is missing.}
}
\end{equation}
What remains is only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{insert the seven same-shell constants and compute }
(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}).
}
\end{equation}
So the branch is two finite microscopic audits away from a fully populated reduced microscopic coefficient point.

\section{Final Summary}

The canonical mixed odd-active branch is now structurally closed.

Its branch data are fixed by
\[
T_E=T_O=1,\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\]
and the only remaining microscopic tasks are exactly two finite audits:

\[
\text{(A) mixed same-shell support insertion},
\qquad
\text{(B) mixed-block transverse cancellation audit}.
\]

If the branch-consistent same-shell support inequality
\[
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\]
holds, if the mixed-block survival condition
\[
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|
\]
holds, and if the primitive longitudinal seed survives
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq0,
\]
then the branch defines a nondegenerate odd-active reduced microscopic carrier.

Its final coefficient point is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
\]

Therefore no new structural theorem is missing.
The branch is two finite microscopic audits away from a fully populated reduced microscopic coefficient point.

\section{Audit A in Fully Executable Form: the Canonical \(TT\) Seven-Constant Table}

\section{Current stage}

For the canonical mixed odd-active branch
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\]
the same-shell support side is already reduced to the branch-consistent inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:A_support_start}
\end{equation}
The only uninserted same-shell data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},
\qquad
L_+^{TT},\ L_-^{TT},\ L_0^{TT},
\qquad
C_+^{TT},\ C_-^{TT},\ C_m^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:A_7unknowns}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Exact canonical \(TT\)-overlap package}

The branch-consistent mixed overlap family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
}
\label{eq:A_STT_general}
\end{equation}
and at \(\varphi=\pi/4\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:A_STT_pi4}
\end{equation}

Therefore the diagonal benchmark quantity is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(0)
=
\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(0)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_Sdiag_exact}
\end{equation}
whenever the valley-symmetric diagonal subcase holds.

\section{2. Exact first-derivative vectors}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:A_ell_defs}
\end{equation}

By linearity of differentiation and \eqref{eq:A_STT_pi4},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{+,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{+,i}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_ell_plus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{-,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{-,i}^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_ell_minus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
=
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
+
\frac12\ell_{0,i}^{OO}
+
\ell_{0,i}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A_ell_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus the three vector-valued derivative packages are exact linear combinations.

\section{3. Norm-level budgets}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:A_L_defs}
\end{equation}

Since norms are not linear, the honest branch-level statement is the triangle-inequality bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_+^{EE}
+
\frac12L_+^{OO}
+
L_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_Lplus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_-^{EE}
+
\frac12L_-^{OO}
+
L_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_Lminus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_0^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_0^{EE}
+
\frac12L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A_L0_bound}
\end{equation}

These three bounds are the correct scalar inputs for the drift budget.

\section{4. Second-derivative remainder constants}

The mixed-branch drift coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{(T)}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{+,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A_aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{(T)}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{-,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A_aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i^{(T)}
=
-a_T\ell_{0,i}^{TT},
\qquad
a_T=\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:A_bi}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A_Aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_-^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
}
\label{eq:A_Aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B^{(T)}
\le
a_TL_0^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:A_B}
\end{equation}

Now define the quadratic Taylor-remainder constants by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le\rho}
\left\|
\nabla_p^2 d_+^{(T)}(p)
\right\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
C_-^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le\rho}
\left\|
\nabla_p^2 d_-^{(T)}(p)
\right\|_{\mathrm{op}},
}
\label{eq:A_Cpm_defs}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le\rho}
\left\|
\nabla_p^2 m^{(T)}(p)
\right\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
}
\label{eq:A_Cm_def}
\end{equation}

Because \(\mathcal S^{TT}\) is linear in \(\mathcal S^{EE},\mathcal S^{OO},\mathcal S^{EO}\), their Hessians add linearly, but the operator norm and supremum produce only a bound:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
\le
\frac12C_+^{EE}
+
\frac12C_+^{OO}
+
C_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_Cplus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_-^{TT}
\le
\frac12C_-^{EE}
+
\frac12C_-^{OO}
+
C_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:A_Cminus_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
\le
\frac12C_m^{EE}
+
\frac12C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:A_Cm_bound}
\end{equation}

\section{5. The fully executable seven-constant table}

The canonical \(TT\) seven-constant package is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{constant} & \text{status} & \text{explicit canonical formula} \\[1mm]
\hline
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
& \text{exact}
&
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\\[2mm]
L_+^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
L_+^{TT}\le
\frac12L_+^{EE}
+\frac12L_+^{OO}
+
L_+^{EO}
\\[2mm]
L_-^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
L_-^{TT}\le
\frac12L_-^{EE}
+\frac12L_-^{OO}
+
L_-^{EO}
\\[2mm]
L_0^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
L_0^{TT}\le
\frac12L_0^{EE}
+\frac12L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO}
\\[2mm]
C_+^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
C_+^{TT}\le
\frac12C_+^{EE}
+\frac12C_+^{OO}
+
C_+^{EO}
\\[2mm]
C_-^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
C_-^{TT}\le
\frac12C_-^{EE}
+\frac12C_-^{OO}
+
C_-^{EO}
\\[2mm]
C_m^{TT}
& \text{bound}
&
C_m^{TT}\le
\frac12C_m^{EE}
+\frac12C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}
\end{array}
}
\]
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:A_7constant_table}
\end{equation}

This is the fully executable same-shell insertion table.

\section{6. Fully inserted drift budget}

The small-\(p\) drift satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{(T)}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{(T)}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{(T)}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2},
}
\label{eq:A_eps_explicit}
\end{equation}
with \(A_+^{(T)},A_-^{(T)},B^{(T)}\) bounded by \eqref{eq:A_Aplus}--\eqref{eq:A_B}.

Therefore the branch-consistent same-shell support inequality becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\right)
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:A_support_fully_inserted}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in locked-core scalar form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\right)
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:A_support_scalar_inserted}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Conditional closure statement for Audit A}

Hence Audit A closes once the \(EE/OO/EO\) scalar packages are inserted into
\eqref{eq:A_7constant_table}.
No new theorem is needed.
The only remaining task is the literal numerical or symbolic insertion of the already-defined
\(EE/OO/EO\) benchmark/Taylor data.

\section{Final Summary}

Audit A is now fully reduced to an explicit insertion table.

For the canonical mixed branch,
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
\]

Hence the diagonal benchmark quantity is exactly
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
\]

Likewise, the derivative vectors satisfy exact linear identities,
while the norm-level quantities
\[
L_+^{TT},\ L_-^{TT},\ L_0^{TT},\ C_+^{TT},\ C_-^{TT},\ C_m^{TT}
\]
are controlled by honest upper bounds.

Therefore the fully inserted same-shell support inequality is
\[
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\right)
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
\]

So Audit A is no longer structurally open.
What remains is only the literal insertion of the already-defined \(EE/OO/EO\) scalar packages.
