\section{Audit B Beyond the Formal Split: a KK-Residual Dominance Reduction}

\section{Short explanation}

At the current stage, the exact transverse extraction is already closed as a blockwise sum:
\[
e_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]
The remaining issue is therefore not how to define the correction pair
\[
(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}),
\]
but how to dominate it sharply enough so that the already explicit \(K\)-sector witness survives.

The strongest further reduction supported by the current notes is a source-level dominance criterion:
the principal transverse source is \(JK+KJ\), while the \(KK\)-sector is residual.

\section{1. Exact principal/residual split}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\bigl(
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:B_rpr}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
:=
\bigl(
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
\bigr)
=
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}
\bigl(
e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:B_rrem}
\end{equation}

Then the full transverse point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\mathrm{pr}}+r_{\mathrm{rem}}.
}
\label{eq:B_fullsplit}
\end{equation}

At the current conservative stage,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\label{eq:B_conservative_split}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Source-level classification}

The exact source-by-source classification is already fixed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK\to \text{transverse residual corrections}.
}
\label{eq:B_source_classification}
\end{equation}

Thus the principal transverse carrier is the mixed \(JK+KJ\) source,
while the \(KK\)-sector should be treated as a correction sector rather than a principal carrier source.

\section{3. Exact quadratic forms in response-vector language}

The exact finite quadratic forms are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_T
=
\alpha_X^2\,\mathcal N_T^{JJ}
+
2\alpha_X\beta_X\,\mathcal N_T^{JK}
+
\beta_X^2\,\mathcal N_T^{KK},
}
\label{eq:B_WT}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_s
=
\alpha_X^2\,\mathcal N_s^{JJ}
+
2\alpha_X\beta_X\,\mathcal N_s^{JK}
+
\beta_X^2\,\mathcal N_s^{KK}.
}
\label{eq:B_Ws}
\end{equation}

Accordingly define the principal transverse weights
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_T^{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
2\alpha_X\beta_X\,\mathcal N_T^{JK},
\qquad
W_s^{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
2\alpha_X\beta_X\,\mathcal N_s^{JK},
}
\label{eq:B_Wpr}
\end{equation}
and the residual \(KK\)-weights
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_T^{\mathrm{KK}}
:=
\beta_X^2\,\mathcal N_T^{KK},
\qquad
W_s^{\mathrm{KK}}
:=
\beta_X^2\,\mathcal N_s^{KK}.
}
\label{eq:B_WKK}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Shell-support sum rule}

For each mixed shell-defect Hessian block \(B\), if the shell-support property holds for the transverse probe, then the exact mixed-sector sum rule is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_{B,+}^2+g_{B,-}^2=g_{s_B}^2.
}
\label{eq:B_sumrule}
\end{equation}

Hence shell-defect mixing cannot enhance the total mixed-sector transverse weight beyond the corresponding shell-slot bare weight.

This gives the sharpest currently available principle for the residual audit:
the \(KK\)-sector may renormalize the transverse pair, but it cannot produce an arbitrarily larger mixed-sector weight than its own bare shell slot.

\section{5. Practical sufficient dominance criterion}

The strong coefficient-level survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:B_strong_coeff}
\end{equation}

A source-level sufficient reduction of this is to demand that the residual \(KK\)-weights be dominated by the principal \(JK\)-weights:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|W_T^{\mathrm{KK}}|<|W_T^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
\qquad
|W_s^{\mathrm{KK}}|<|W_s^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:B_source_dominance_component}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X^2|\mathcal N_T^{KK}|
<
2|\alpha_X\beta_X|\,|\mathcal N_T^{JK}|,
\qquad
\beta_X^2|\mathcal N_s^{KK}|
<
2|\alpha_X\beta_X|\,|\mathcal N_s^{JK}|.
}
\label{eq:B_source_dominance_explicit}
\end{equation}

A rotationally invariant combined sufficient criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sqrt{
\bigl(W_T^{\mathrm{KK}}\bigr)^2+
\bigl(W_s^{\mathrm{KK}}\bigr)^2
}
<
\sqrt{
\bigl(W_T^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr)^2+
\bigl(W_s^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr)^2
}.
}
\label{eq:B_source_dominance_Euclid}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Honest status.}
The inequalities \eqref{eq:B_source_dominance_component}--\eqref{eq:B_source_dominance_Euclid} are not exact identities between
\[
(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}})
\quad\text{and}\quad
(W_T^{\mathrm{KK}},W_s^{\mathrm{KK}}),
\]
but they are the strongest source-level sufficient dominance criteria currently justified by the exact response-weight decomposition and shell-support sum rule.

\section{6. Exchange-symmetric residual simplification}

If the projected residual sector preserves
\[
O\leftrightarrow D
\]
exchange symmetry, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:B_ODDO_equal}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:B_rrem_reduced}
\end{equation}

So once exchange symmetry is imposed, Audit B reduces to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one \(OD\)-pair,
\item one \(DD\)-pair,
\item the \(KK\)-dominance comparison against the principal \(JK\)-pair.
\end{enumerate}

\section{7. Conditional final reduction of Audit B}

Therefore the sharpest current practical reduction of Audit B is the following:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Audit B closes if either the coefficient-level strong condition \eqref{eq:B_strong_coeff} is checked directly,}
}
\end{equation}
or, more conservatively,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the source-level \(KK\)-dominance bounds \eqref{eq:B_source_dominance_explicit} or \eqref{eq:B_source_dominance_Euclid} are satisfied.}
}
\end{equation}

In that case the already explicit \(K\)-sector witness pair survives, and hence
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
\]

\section{8. Final mixed-branch coefficient point under the two audits}

Once Audit A is inserted and Audit B passes, the final mixed-branch microscopic coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:B_final_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:B_final_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:B_final_beta}
\end{equation}
So no new structural theorem remains.
What remains is only literal finite insertion and comparison.

\section{Final Summary}

The sharpest further reduction of Audit B supported by the current notes is a source-level dominance criterion.

The exact source classification is
\[
JJ\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK\to \text{transverse residual corrections}.
\]

Therefore the principal transverse weights are
\[
W_T^{\mathrm{pr}}=2\alpha_X\beta_X\,\mathcal N_T^{JK},
\qquad
W_s^{\mathrm{pr}}=2\alpha_X\beta_X\,\mathcal N_s^{JK},
\]
while the residual \(KK\)-weights are
\[
W_T^{\mathrm{KK}}=\beta_X^2\,\mathcal N_T^{KK},
\qquad
W_s^{\mathrm{KK}}=\beta_X^2\,\mathcal N_s^{KK}.
\]

A practical sufficient condition for residual non-cancellation is
\[
\beta_X^2|\mathcal N_T^{KK}|
<
2|\alpha_X\beta_X|\,|\mathcal N_T^{JK}|,
\qquad
\beta_X^2|\mathcal N_s^{KK}|
<
2|\alpha_X\beta_X|\,|\mathcal N_s^{JK}|.
\]

Equivalently, in Euclidean form,
\[
\sqrt{(W_T^{\mathrm{KK}})^2+(W_s^{\mathrm{KK}})^2}
<
\sqrt{(W_T^{\mathrm{pr}})^2+(W_s^{\mathrm{pr}})^2}.
\]

If, in addition, the residual sector preserves \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, then
\[
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr),
\]
so Audit B reduces to one \(OD\)-pair, one \(DD\)-pair, and one \(KK\)-dominance comparison.

Thus the branch is now reduced to:
one same-shell finite insertion audit, and one source-level residual dominance audit.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Audit B as an Explicit Source-Split Coefficient Formula}

\section{Short explanation}

The strongest further reduction of Audit B is not another abstract survival statement.
It is the explicit source-split formula for the transverse coefficients themselves.

The exact Schur-corrected effective operator already has the source decomposition
\[
\Delta H_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}(\delta J\delta J^\dagger)
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\delta K\delta K^\dagger).
\]
Therefore every reduced coefficient splits into \(JJ\), \(JK+KJ\), and \(KK\) pieces.

\section{1. Exact source decomposition of the reduced coefficients}

The reduced invariants satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK},
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\alpha
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK},
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\beta
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}.
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_beta}
\end{equation}

Now insert the already-closed routing logic:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{JJ}=\Lambda_O^{JJ}=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_c^{JK}=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_c^{KK}=0
\quad
\text{at principal shell order.}
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_routing_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal reduced source structure collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\sim \lambda_c^{JJ},
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_lcJJ}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
\sim
\Lambda_E^{JK}+\Lambda_E^{KK},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
\sim
\Lambda_O^{JK}+\Lambda_O^{KK}.
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_LambdaEOKK}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit mixed-branch coefficient formulas}

After overlap insertion, the canonical mixed-branch coefficient dictionary is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Using \eqref{eq:srcsplit_lcJJ} and \eqref{eq:srcsplit_LambdaEOKK}, one gets the sharper source-split formulas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Lambda_c^{JJ}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_final_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_final_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_final_beta}
\end{equation}

These are more explicit than the earlier
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr),
\]
because they identify the principal source and the residual source separately.

\section{3. Identification of the principal and residual transverse pieces}

Comparing \eqref{eq:srcsplit_final_alpha}--\eqref{eq:srcsplit_final_beta} with the conservative mixed-branch form, one may identify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK},
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_Kpiece}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
\sim
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
\sim
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK},
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_mixpiece}
\end{equation}
at the source-classification level.

\paragraph{Honest status.}
These are not exact equalities block-by-block in the already-expanded
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD
\]
basis.
They are the sharpest source-level identifications currently justified by the exact Schur split and the already-closed routing logic.

\section{4. Practical dominance criteria}

The strong coefficient-level survival condition
\[
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|
\]
is therefore implied by the explicit source-level inequalities
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right|
<
\left|
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
\right|,
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_domE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right|
<
\left|
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_domO}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_E^{KK}|<|\alpha_X|\,|\Lambda_E^{JK}|,
\qquad
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_O^{KK}|<|\alpha_X|\,|\Lambda_O^{JK}|.
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_dom_simple}
\end{equation}

A rotationally invariant sufficient version is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{KK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{KK})^2}
<
|\alpha_X|\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{JK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{JK})^2}.
}
\label{eq:srcsplit_dom_Euclid}
\end{equation}

\section{5. What this means for the mixed odd-active branch}

Thus the canonical mixed odd-active branch closes once the following hold:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the same-shell support inequality from Audit A;
\item the longitudinal primitive seed
\[
\Lambda_c^{JJ}\neq0;
\]
\item the mixed-source transverse pair survives
\[
(\Lambda_E^{JK},\Lambda_O^{JK})\neq(0,0);
\]
\item the \(KK\)-residual is dominated by the \(JK\)-source in the sense of
\eqref{eq:srcsplit_dom_simple} or \eqref{eq:srcsplit_dom_Euclid}.
\end{enumerate}

Under these conditions the final coefficient point is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Lambda_c^{JJ}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
\]
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
\]

So Audit B is no longer an amorphous mixed-block remainder.
It is a concrete comparison between a principal \(JK\)-pair and a residual \(KK\)-pair.

\section{Final Summary}

Audit B can now be reduced to an explicit source-split coefficient formula.

Using the exact Schur decomposition and the already-closed routing logic,
the longitudinal coefficient is sourced only by the \(JJ\)-sector:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Lambda_c^{JJ}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

The transverse coefficients split into a principal \(JK\)-pair and a residual \(KK\)-pair:
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
\]
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
\]

Therefore Audit B is no longer an undifferentiated mixed-block correction problem.
It is a concrete competition between the principal \(JK\)-source and the residual \(KK\)-source.

A practical sufficient dominance criterion is
\[
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_E^{KK}|<|\alpha_X|\,|\Lambda_E^{JK}|,
\qquad
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_O^{KK}|<|\alpha_X|\,|\Lambda_O^{JK}|,
\]
or equivalently
\[
|\beta_X|\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{KK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{KK})^2}
<
|\alpha_X|\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{JK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{JK})^2}.
\]

Hence the canonical mixed odd-active branch closes once:
same-shell support holds,
the longitudinal \(JJ\)-seed survives,
the principal \(JK\)-transverse pair is nonzero,
and the residual \(KK\)-pair is dominated by the \(JK\)-pair.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit \(JK\)-Driven Principal Transverse Coefficients on the Frozen Corrected Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

The source routing was already known:
\[
JJ\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ\to(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK\to \text{transverse residual corrections}.
\]
The genuinely new forward step is that, on the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch,
the \(JK\)-driven principal transverse pair is already reduced to an explicit finite contraction.

\section{1. Background currents}

On the locked one-defect background
\[
\Psi_B(\xi,x_\parallel)=\phi_0(x_\parallel)\,z_B(\xi),
\qquad
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B^\dagger(\xi),
\]
the microscopic currents are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\,\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta'),
}
\label{eq:JK_J_background}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_a(\theta)=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\qquad
\mathcal A_\xi^a
=
(\partial_\xi z_B^\dagger)T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a(\partial_\xi z_B),
}
\label{eq:JK_mA_defs}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\qquad
k_a(\theta):=\Tr\!\Bigl[T_a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:JK_K_background}
\end{equation}

Thus the background \(J\)-sector carries the shell gradient, while the \(K\)-sector carries the defect/projector derivative.

\section{2. Principal \(JK\)-pair}

At the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the mixed \(JK+KJ\) source yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,(j\!\cdot\!k)\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
c_O
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,(j\!\cdot\!k)\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:JK_ceco_explicit}
\end{equation}

Hence the principal transverse pair may be identified as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{JK}
=
(j\!\cdot\!k)\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{JK}
=
(j\!\cdot\!k)\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:JK_Lambda0_identification}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest explicit source-level reduction currently available for the principal transverse source.

\section{3. Mixed-branch coefficient formulas with explicit \(JK\)-pair}

The exact reduced coefficient dictionary is
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]
Separating principal \(JK\) and residual \(KK\) pieces, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
}
\label{eq:JK_alpha_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
}
\label{eq:JK_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

So the principal/transverse competition is now completely explicit:
\[
\text{principal }JK
\;\;\text{vs.}\;\;
\text{residual }KK.
\]

\section{4. Sharp practical dominance criterion}

The \(KK\)-residual cannot kill the principal transverse pair if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_E^{KK}|
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|\,|\Lambda_E^{(0)}|,
}
\label{eq:JK_domE_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_O^{KK}|
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|\,|\Lambda_O^{(0)}|.
}
\label{eq:JK_domO_explicit}
\end{equation}

A rotationally invariant sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{KK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{KK})^2}
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|\,
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2+(\Lambda_O^{(0)})^2}.
}
\label{eq:JK_domEuclid_explicit}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest currently justified scalar dominance cut for Audit B.

\section{5. Honest odd-channel status}

There is one important caveat.
The simplest local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear can vanish identically by Pauli anticommutation,
so a nonzero odd transverse witness is not automatic from the naive local shortcut alone.
Moreover, at the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0,
\]
so orbit-amplitude corrections alone do not activate the odd channel.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\neq0
\ \text{requires genuinely derivative-resolved and/or phase-resolved microscopic structure.}
}
\label{eq:JK_odd_caveat}
\end{equation}

So the honest remaining transverse frontier is not the whole \(JK\)-pair,
but specifically the explicit activation of the odd slot.

\section{6. Final mixed-branch source-split coefficients}

Combining the already-closed longitudinal source with the new principal \(JK\)-pair, the mixed odd-active branch coefficient point is now reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Lambda_c^{JJ}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:JK_final_lpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
}
\label{eq:JK_final_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
}
\label{eq:JK_final_beta}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest explicitly source-split form currently available.

\section{Conclusion}

The principal transverse source is no longer abstract.
It is controlled by the finite background contraction
\[
(j\!\cdot\!k)
\]
and the shell-doublet invariants
\[
\Lambda_E^{(0)},\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

So the remaining literal microscopic tasks are now exactly:
\begin{enumerate}
\item evaluate \(j\!\cdot\!k\) on the frozen corrected branch;
\item determine whether \(\Lambda_O^{(0)}\) is activated by the genuinely derivative/phase-resolved microscopic slot;
\item estimate \((\Lambda_E^{KK},\Lambda_O^{KK})\) and check the dominance inequality.
\end{enumerate}
No larger structural ambiguity remains.

\section{Final Summary}

The principal transverse \(JK\)-source is now reduced to an explicit finite contraction on the frozen corrected branch:
\[
\Lambda_E^{JK}=(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{JK}=(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Therefore the mixed odd-active branch coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Lambda_c^{JJ}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
\]
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
\]

A practical sufficient residual-dominance condition is
\[
|\beta_X|\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{KK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{KK})^2}
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|\,
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2+(\Lambda_O^{(0)})^2}.
\]

So the remaining literal microscopic tasks are:
evaluate \(j\!\cdot\!k\),
determine whether \(\Lambda_O^{(0)}\) is actually activated,
and estimate the residual \(KK\)-pair.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Microscopic Activation Route for the Odd Transverse Slot}

\section{Current stage}

The remaining sharp microscopic question is not whether an odd transverse slot is logically allowed.
That has already been established.

The actual question is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{what is the \emph{minimal} microscopic slot that activates }\Lambda_O^{(0)}\text{ on the intended branch?}
}
\end{equation}

The honest answer splits into two different notions:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal odd source \emph{inside the current frozen corrected Class II working branch};
\item the minimal odd source \emph{after enlarging the complete action by an explicit odd carrier slot}.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Why the naive local \(JK\) route is not the answer}

At the shell-adapted Pauli level,
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2.
\]
Then the naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=0
}
\label{eq:odd_naive_JK_zero}
\end{equation}
by Pauli anticommutation.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the naive local real Hermitian }JK\text{ bilinear does \emph{not} activate }\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:odd_naive_not_answer}
\end{equation}

So a nonzero odd transverse coefficient cannot be claimed from a local algebraic shortcut.
A genuinely nonzero odd channel requires derivative-resolved and/or phase-resolved microscopic structure.

\section{2. First active odd source on the frozen corrected branch}

The exact odd transverse source on the current working branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_2(\delta)
=
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}(\delta)
\right].
}
\label{eq:odd_X2_def}
\end{equation}

Its corrected odd transverse Hessian response is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
:=
\partial_{\delta_r}\partial_{\delta_s}
X_2(\delta)\big|_{\delta=0}
=
\partial_{\delta_r}\partial_{\delta_s}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}(\delta)
\right]_{\delta=0}.
}
\label{eq:odd_H2_def}
\end{equation}

On the refined locked \(+\) Class II frozen working branch, the leading mixed-channel realization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\text{subleading completion terms}.
}
\label{eq:odd_H2_JK}
\end{equation}

Moreover, on the sign-resolved first-shell lift of the frozen corrected seed,
the exact transverse rows satisfy
\[
r^{(ct_1)}_{\rm sub}\!\cdot\!\delta_{\rm sub}^{\rm corr}=0,
\qquad
r^{(ct_2)}_{\rm sub}\!\cdot\!\delta_{\rm sub}^{\rm corr}=0.
\]
Hence there is no linear odd transverse activation at the frozen corrected seed.

Therefore the first genuine odd source on the current branch is not linear but quadratic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\ \text{first appears through the quadratic Hessian response }H^{(2)}_{rs}.
}
\label{eq:odd_first_genuine_source}
\end{equation}

At the level of the corrected branch displacement \(\delta^{\rm corr}\), the natural leading-order estimate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\sim
\frac12\,\delta_r^{\rm corr}\,H^{(2)}_{rs}\,\delta_s^{\rm corr},
}
\label{eq:odd_quadratic_estimate}
\end{equation}
up to higher-order completion terms.
This is an inference from the Hessian-response definition and the absence of linear activation.

\section{3. The minimal odd slot after complete-action enlargement}

The complete mixing sector can include an explicit odd carrier slot
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
\supset
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O+\mathrm{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:odd_complete_slot}
\end{equation}
in addition to the \(J\)- and \(K\)-couplings.

On the embedded defect branch,
\[
q_O(\theta)=\Tr(S_OM_O)=\cos\theta,
\]
so the explicit odd carrier density is locally nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:odd_IO_local}
\end{equation}

The induced tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:odd_VEO}
\end{equation}
Hence the local odd density is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O^{(EO)}
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:odd_bO_local}
\end{equation}

Therefore, in the enlarged complete-action sense,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the minimal \emph{linear} odd microscopic slot is the explicit odd carrier }\mathcal I_O.
}
\label{eq:odd_minimal_linear_slot}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Honest two-route conclusion}

We can now distinguish the two notions sharply:

\paragraph{(A) Minimal odd source inside the current frozen corrected branch.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{quadratic mixed }JK+KJ\text{ Hessian response }H^{(2)}_{rs}.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_A}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(B) Minimal odd source after complete-action enlargement.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{explicit odd carrier slot }\mathcal I_O
\text{ generating }V_{EO}^\mu
\propto \theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_B}
\end{equation}

So the current branch and the completed action do not have the same minimal odd activation mechanism.

\section{5. Consequence for the mixed odd-active coefficient sheet}

Accordingly, the odd coefficient in the mixed odd-active branch can be written in two logically distinct ways.

\paragraph{Current frozen corrected branch.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right],
}
\label{eq:odd_beta_current_branch}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\sim
\frac12\delta_r^{\rm corr}H^{(2)}_{rs}\delta_s^{\rm corr}
\]
as the first genuinely active odd source.

\paragraph{Enlarged complete-action route.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(EO)}
\right],
}
\label{eq:odd_beta_complete_route}
\end{equation}
where \(\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(EO)}\) is the coefficient induced by the explicit odd carrier slot.

\section{Conclusion}

The minimal microscopic activation route for the odd transverse slot is now sharply identified:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the current branch: quadratic Hessian response;}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the enlarged complete action: explicit odd carrier } \mathcal I_O.
}
\end{equation}

So the real remaining microscopic frontier is no longer “does an odd slot exist?”
It is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{which of these two routes is actually realized in the physically intended complete TECT branch?}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The minimal microscopic activation mechanism for the odd transverse slot is now sharply separated into two routes.

Inside the current frozen corrected Class II working branch, the naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear vanishes.
There is no linear odd activation at the frozen corrected seed.
Hence the first genuinely active odd source is the quadratic Hessian response
\[
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\cdots,
\]
so that
\[
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\sim
\frac12\delta_r^{\rm corr}H^{(2)}_{rs}\delta_s^{\rm corr}.
\]

By contrast, after enlarging the complete action, the explicit odd carrier slot
\[
\gamma_O\mathcal I_O
\]
provides a linear odd route through
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\]
with local odd density
\[
b_O^{(EO)}
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

Therefore the true remaining microscopic frontier is not the existence of an odd slot,
but which of these two activation routes is physically realized in the intended complete TECT branch.

\section{Actual Contraction of the Odd Hessian Response on the Frozen Corrected Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

The corrected branch is frozen at
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62),
\qquad
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(\delta_A,\delta_E,\delta_O)=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096).
\]
The odd transverse coefficient starts at quadratic order:
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,Q_2(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
+
O(\delta^3).
\]
So the correct next step is to contract the quadratic form explicitly.

\section{1. Exact quadratic contraction on \(\delta^{\mathrm{final}}\)}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta)
=
\frac12
\sum_{r,s\in\{A,E,O\}}
H^{(2)}_{rs}\,\delta_r\delta_s.
}
\label{eq:Q2_def_exec}
\end{equation}

For
\[
\delta_A=\delta_O=d,\qquad
\delta_E=-3d,
\qquad
d=0.0096,
\]
one has
\[
d^2=9.216\times10^{-5}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{align}
Q_2(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
&=
\frac{d^2}{2}
\Bigl[
H^{(2)}_{AA}
+9H^{(2)}_{EE}
+H^{(2)}_{OO}
-6H^{(2)}_{AE}
+2H^{(2)}_{AO}
-6H^{(2)}_{EO}
\Bigr]
\\
&=
4.608\times10^{-5}
\Bigl[
H^{(2)}_{AA}
+9H^{(2)}_{EE}
+H^{(2)}_{OO}
-6H^{(2)}_{AE}
+2H^{(2)}_{AO}
-6H^{(2)}_{EO}
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Q2_contracted_exact}
\end{align}

Define the contracted odd Hessian combination
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}
:=
H^{(2)}_{AA}
+9H^{(2)}_{EE}
+H^{(2)}_{OO}
-6H^{(2)}_{AE}
+2H^{(2)}_{AO}
-6H^{(2)}_{EO}.
}
\label{eq:Hodd_contracted}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}\,
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}.
}
\label{eq:Q2_Hodd}
\end{equation}

Hence the corrected odd coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
(4.608\times10^{-5})\,\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:beta_corr_Hodd}
\end{equation}

So the odd slot is activated on the frozen corrected branch if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:odd_activation_iff}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact six-row microscopic formula}

The common exact working-branch definition of the six Hessian rows is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
J_{rs}K_0^\dagger
+
J_rK_s^\dagger
+
J_sK_r^\dagger
+
J_0K_{rs}^\dagger
+
K_{rs}J_0^\dagger
+
K_rJ_s^\dagger
+
K_sJ_r^\dagger
+
K_0J_{rs}^\dagger
\Big]
+\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{rs}.
}
\label{eq:H2_master_exec}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:H2_master_exec} into \eqref{eq:Hodd_contracted}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak X_O
+
\mathfrak D_O,
}
\label{eq:Hodd_source_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak X_O
:=
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\mathcal C_{AA}
+9\mathcal C_{EE}
+\mathcal C_{OO}
-6\mathcal C_{AE}
+2\mathcal C_{AO}
-6\mathcal C_{EO}
\Big],
}
\label{eq:Xodd_def}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{rs}
:=
J_{rs}K_0^\dagger
+
J_rK_s^\dagger
+
J_sK_r^\dagger
+
J_0K_{rs}^\dagger
+
K_{rs}J_0^\dagger
+
K_rJ_s^\dagger
+
K_sJ_r^\dagger
+
K_0J_{rs}^\dagger,
}
\label{eq:Crs_def}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak D_O
:=
\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{AA}
+9\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{EE}
+\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{OO}
-6\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{AE}
+2\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{AO}
-6\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{EO}.
}
\label{eq:Dodd_def}
\end{equation}

Therefore the corrected odd coefficient becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
(4.608\times10^{-5})
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak X_O
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
(4.608\times10^{-5})\,
\mathfrak D_O
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:beta_corr_source_split}
\end{equation}

This is the fully contracted source-split odd-slot formula on the frozen corrected branch.

\section{3. Fast practical approximation}

Under the fast practical approximation
\[
J_{rs}\approx0,\qquad
K_{rs}\approx0,\qquad
\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{rs}\approx0,
\]
all six rows reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{rs}
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_rK_s^\dagger+J_sK_r^\dagger+K_rJ_s^\dagger+K_sJ_r^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:Hfast_general}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{fast}}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak X_O^{\mathrm{fast}},
}
\label{eq:Hodd_fast}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak X_O^{\mathrm{fast}}
:=
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\mathcal B_{AA}
+9\mathcal B_{EE}
+\mathcal B_{OO}
-6\mathcal B_{AE}
+2\mathcal B_{AO}
-6\mathcal B_{EO}
\Big],
}
\label{eq:Xodd_fast_def}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{rs}
:=
J_rK_s^\dagger+J_sK_r^\dagger+K_rJ_s^\dagger+K_sJ_r^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:Brs_def}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}_{\mathrm{fast}}
\approx
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
(4.608\times10^{-5})
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak X_O^{\mathrm{fast}}.
}
\label{eq:beta_corr_fast}
\end{equation}

So even in the fast approximation, the odd-slot question has been reduced to one scalar:
\[
\mathfrak X_O^{\mathrm{fast}}.
\]

\section{4. A clean sufficient nonzero criterion}

A sharp sufficient condition for odd-slot activation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\mathfrak X_O
\right|
>
|\mathfrak D_O|.
}
\label{eq:odd_activation_strong}
\end{equation}
Indeed, under \eqref{eq:Hodd_source_split}, this implies
\[
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}\neq0
\]
and therefore \(\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\neq0\) up to the overall prefactor
\(\theta_0\kappa A_0\neq0\).

In the fast approximation this reduces simply to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak X_O^{\mathrm{fast}}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}_{\mathrm{fast}}\neq0
}
\label{eq:odd_activation_fast}
\end{equation}
provided
\[
\alpha_X\beta_X\theta_0\kappa A_0\neq0.
\]

\section{5. A useful dominance cut directly on the six rows}

Because the \(EE\)-entry carries the largest weight \(9\), one convenient sufficient criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|H^{(2)}_{EE}|
>
\frac19\bigl(|H^{(2)}_{AA}|+|H^{(2)}_{OO}|\bigr)
+\frac23\bigl(|H^{(2)}_{AE}|+|H^{(2)}_{EO}|\bigr)
+\frac29|H^{(2)}_{AO}|.
}
\label{eq:odd_EE_dominance}
\end{equation}
If, moreover, the signs are such that the \(EE\)-term contributes constructively, then
\[
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}\neq0.
\]

This is not necessary, but it is a practical row-level sufficient test.

\section{6. Honest status relative to earlier truncations}

At the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation one had
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0,
\]
so orbit-amplitude corrections alone do not activate the odd witness.

The present formula is stronger:
it shows exactly where the first nonzero odd response can appear on the corrected branch, namely in the contracted six-row Hessian combination \(\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}\).

So the odd-slot frontier is no longer vague.
It is a literal six-row microscopic overlap table, or one scalar contraction thereof.

\section{Final Summary}

On the frozen corrected branch
\[
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
the odd transverse response has now been fully contracted.

The quadratic odd response is
\[
Q_2(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}
\Bigl[
H^{(2)}_{AA}+9H^{(2)}_{EE}+H^{(2)}_{OO}-6H^{(2)}_{AE}+2H^{(2)}_{AO}-6H^{(2)}_{EO}
\Bigr].
\]

Hence
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa A_0
(4.608\times10^{-5})\,
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}
+
O(\delta^3),
\]
with
\[
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
H^{(2)}_{AA}+9H^{(2)}_{EE}+H^{(2)}_{OO}-6H^{(2)}_{AE}+2H^{(2)}_{AO}-6H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]

Using the exact six-row source formula,
\[
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak P_O[\cdots]+\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{rs},
\]
this becomes
\[
\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\mathfrak X_O+\mathfrak D_O.
\]

Therefore a sharp sufficient odd-slot activation criterion is
\[
\left|
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\mathfrak X_O
\right|
>
|\mathfrak D_O|.
\]

So the odd transverse frontier is no longer vague:
it is a literal six-row microscopic overlap table,
or equivalently one contracted scalar \(\mathfrak H_O^{\mathrm{corr}}\).

\section{Actual First Nonzero Odd Route: Fixing the \(E\)-Sector as the Decisive Microscopic Test}

\section{Short explanation}

At this point the odd-slot frontier is no longer a general six-row ambiguity.
The hierarchy is already fixed.

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\[
K_A=K_E=K_O=0,
\]
hence all fast six-row coefficients vanish identically and therefore
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,\qquad \beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

So the only way forward is to leave the rigid truncation.
Once this is done, the corrected odd shift is dominated first by \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\), then by \(H^{(2)}_{AE}\) and \(H^{(2)}_{EO}\).

\section{1. Fast six-row system}

Under the fast working approximation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_rK_s^\dagger+J_sK_r^\dagger+K_rJ_s^\dagger+K_sJ_r^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:odd_fast_master_again}
\end{equation}

Therefore, explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big],
}
\label{eq:odd_HEE_fast}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_AK_E^\dagger+J_EK_A^\dagger+K_AJ_E^\dagger+K_EJ_A^\dagger
\big],
}
\label{eq:odd_HAE_fast}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_O^\dagger+J_OK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_O^\dagger+K_OJ_E^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:odd_HEO_fast}
\end{equation}

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_AK_A^\dagger+K_AJ_A^\dagger
\big],
}
\label{eq:odd_HAA_fast}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_OK_O^\dagger+K_OJ_O^\dagger
\big],
}
\label{eq:odd_HOO_fast}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_AK_O^\dagger+J_OK_A^\dagger+K_AJ_O^\dagger+K_OJ_A^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:odd_HAO_fast}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Why the rigid truncation must be abandoned}

The completed orbit-current pairs are explicit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{r,i}^a
=
q_0^a\,\partial_iN_r
+
(\partial_i\bar\rho)(\eta_r c^a+\bar\eta_r\bar c^a)
+
\bar\rho(c^a\partial_i\eta_r+\bar c^a\partial_i\bar\eta_r),
}
\label{eq:odd_Jr_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{r,i}^a
=
(c^a\partial_i\eta_r+\bar c^a\partial_i\bar\eta_r)\bar\chi
}
\label{eq:odd_Kr_explicit}
\end{equation}
in the non-rigid completion picture. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

But in the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation one has
\[
Q_r^a=0
\qquad
\forall r\in\{A,E,O\},
\]
hence
\[
K_A=K_E=K_O=0.
\]
Therefore every fast coefficient vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
0,
}
\label{eq:odd_all_fast_zero}
\end{equation}
and consequently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
}
\label{eq:odd_rigid_zero_final}
\end{equation}

So the first genuine microscopic conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{odd-slot activation is impossible unless one leaves the rigid first-shell truncation.}
}
\label{eq:odd_leave_rigid}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Weight hierarchy fixes the priority order}

On the frozen corrected branch,
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
the corrected odd shift is
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]

Hence the exact weight hierarchy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|EE|:|AE|:|EO|:|AO|:|AA|:|OO|=9:6:6:2:1:1.
}
\label{eq:odd_weight_hierarchy}
\end{equation}

Therefore the correct microscopic priority order is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}\ \text{first},
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{AE},\ H^{(2)}_{EO}\ \text{second},
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{AO}\ \text{third}.
}
\label{eq:odd_priority_order_final}
\end{equation}

So the first decisive test for whether \(\Lambda_O\neq0\) beyond the rigid truncation is not the whole six-row system but the single coefficient \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\).

\section{4. Exact \(E\)-sector source split}

The exact non-rigid \(E\)-sector current pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_iM_E^a,
}
\label{eq:odd_JE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:odd_KE}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\label{eq:odd_HEE_split_again}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\ \text{comes from}\ 
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi,
}
\label{eq:odd_HEE_proj}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
\ \text{comes from}\ 
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:odd_HEE_qgrad}
\end{equation}

Hence the first nonzero odd transverse source beyond the rigid truncation can come from either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iF_E^a\neq0
\quad\text{(non-rigid internal/projector texture),}
}
\label{eq:odd_proj_route}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a\neq0
\quad\text{(background charge-gradient source).}
}
\label{eq:odd_qgrad_route}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Sharp sufficient criterion for the first nonzero odd slot}

A practical sufficient condition for first odd activation is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\neq0
\ \text{unless the subleading rows cancel it with the tuned opposite sign.}
}
\label{eq:odd_HEE_sufficient}
\end{equation}

A stronger row-dominance version is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|H^{(2)}_{EE}|
>
\max\left\{
\frac{2.7648}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{AE}|,
\frac{2.7648}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{EO}|,
\frac{0.9216}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{AO}|,
\frac{0.4608}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{AA}|,
\frac{0.4608}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{OO}|
\right\},
}
\label{eq:odd_HEE_dominance}
\end{equation}
which implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)H^{(2)}_{EE}.
}
\label{eq:odd_beta_from_HEE}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

So the actual next microscopic calculation is uniquely fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{leave the rigid truncation, compute }(J_E,K_E),\text{ and test }H^{(2)}_{EE}\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

If \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\neq0\), then the odd slot is activated generically before any full six-row computation is required.
The six-row system is still exact, but the \(E\)-sector is the first decisive microscopic test.

\section{Final Summary}

The odd-slot frontier is now sharply localized.

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\[
K_A=K_E=K_O=0,
\]
so
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
0,
\]
and therefore
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

Hence odd-slot activation is impossible unless the rigid truncation is abandoned.

Beyond that truncation, the corrected odd shift carries the exact weight hierarchy
\[
|EE|:|AE|:|EO|:|AO|:|AA|:|OO|=9:6:6:2:1:1,
\]
so the first decisive microscopic test is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE}.
\]

The exact non-rigid \(E\)-sector current pair is
\[
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_iM_E^a,
\qquad
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
\]

Therefore the first nonzero odd transverse source can come from either
\[
\partial_iF_E^a\neq0
\quad\text{(projector/internal texture),}
\]
or
\[
\partial_i\bar q^a\neq0
\quad\text{(background charge-gradient source).}
\]

So the next unique microscopic task is:
leave the rigid truncation, compute the \(E\)-sector pair \((J_E,K_E)\), and test whether \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\neq0\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{First Actual Decision Between the Two \(E\)-Sector Odd Sources}

\section{Short explanation}

The rigid first-shell truncation is already dead for the odd channel:
\[
K_A=K_E=K_O=0
\Longrightarrow
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
0,
\]
hence
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

So the actual odd-slot question begins only beyond the rigid truncation.
At that point, the first decisive coefficient is \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\), and it splits into
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
\]

\section{1. Exact \(E\)-sector split}

The exact fast \(E\)-sector coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_fast_exact}
\end{equation}

The completed \(E\)-sector orbit-current pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_iM_E^a,
}
\label{eq:Esrc_JE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_KE}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\propto
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\Big],
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_proj}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
\propto
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\Big].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_qgrad}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Which source is first generic?}

The projector/internal-texture piece \eqref{eq:Esrc_HEE_proj} requires
\[
\partial_iQ_E^a\neq0,
\]
that is, genuinely non-rigid internal/projector texture.

By contrast, the q-gradient piece \eqref{eq:Esrc_HEE_qgrad} is already carried by the defect background itself,
through the background charge gradient and the defect profile:
\[
\partial_\xi M_E^a,
\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\theta m_a(\theta).
\]

Therefore the first generic candidate is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_first_generic}
\end{equation}

This is precisely why, once the rigid truncation is abandoned, the corrected odd coefficient is led by the q-gradient \(E\)-sector source.

\section{3. Weighted insertion into the corrected odd coefficient}

For the frozen corrected seed
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
the corrected odd shift is
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]
Since the \(EE\)-slot carries the largest weight, once no large cancellation occurs,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_beta_dominant}
\end{equation}

So the first actual odd activation test is reduced to the sign and nonvanishing of \(H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}\).

\section{4. Fully explicit shell-overlap form}

The q-gradient route has already been reduced to a literal shell-overlap test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{4}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_beta_shell_overlap}
\end{equation}

Therefore the literal frozen-branch odd decision is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right]
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_final_overlap_test}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Honest practical conclusion}

So there are now two different honest forward routes:

\paragraph{Route A: stay inside the current \(JK\)-route.}
Then the first generic odd source is \(H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}\), and the final decision is the finite shell-overlap test \eqref{eq:Esrc_final_overlap_test}.
This still requires the actual frozen branch harmonics
\[
\bar A_G,\qquad B_G^{(E)}.
\]

\paragraph{Route B: move to the explicit odd extra-carrier route.}
Then the odd slot is explicitly present already at lowest order through
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi,
}
\label{eq:Esrc_IO}
\end{equation}
with induced tangent transport block
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_VEO}
\end{equation}
So the odd transport density is directly nonzero whenever
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0,\qquad
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0,\qquad
\cos\theta(\xi)\not\equiv0.
\]

\section{Conclusion}

Inside the current frozen corrected branch, the first generic odd source is the \(E\)-sector q-gradient term:
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\]
But its literal sign test still requires the unavailable frozen harmonics.

Therefore the honest status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{current \(JK\)-route: reduced to one finite shell-overlap test;}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{explicit extra-carrier route: already forward-computable and explicitly odd at lowest order.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Inside the current frozen corrected branch, the first generic odd source is not the projector/internal-texture term but the \(E\)-sector q-gradient term:
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\]

Accordingly, the corrected odd coefficient is led by
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
\]

Moreover, the \(JK\)-route has already been reduced to a single literal shell-overlap test:
\[
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right]
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

So the current \(JK\)-route is no longer structurally vague.
It is one finite shell-overlap decision.

However, this test still requires the actual frozen branch harmonics
\[
\bar A_G,\qquad B_G^{(E)},
\]
which are not instantiated in the present context.

Therefore the honest forward-computable route at the current stage is the explicit odd extra-carrier route, where
\[
\mathcal I_O=X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi
\]
induces
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\]
and hence gives a directly nonzero odd transport density whenever
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0,\qquad
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0,\qquad
\cos\theta(\xi)\not\equiv0.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Adopting the Explicit Odd Extra-Carrier Route as the Active Forward Closure}

\section{Current stage}

The \(JK\)-route has already been reduced to a single shell-overlap decision, but that literal sign test still requires unavailable frozen harmonics. Therefore the correct forward move is not to stall there, but to switch to the already explicit odd extra-carrier route.

The complete minimal extra mixing sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O
+
\mathrm{h.c.},
}
\label{eq:extra_mix_minimal_active}
\end{equation}
with the odd transverse carrier slot
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\mathcal O^{ia}[P,\Psi,\sigma].
}
\label{eq:slot_O_active}
\end{equation}

This slot is not optional at the level of complete first-order principal-symbol closure: the complete action needs one independent generator for each of the three carrier directions \(L,E,O\).

\section{1. Explicit odd carrier on the embedded defect branch}

On the embedded defect branch one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_O(\theta)=\Tr(S_O M_O)=\cos\theta.
}
\label{eq:qO_cos}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit odd extra carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:IO_explicit}
\end{equation}

Hence the odd carrier is locally nonzero whenever
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\cos\theta(\xi)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:IO_local_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Induced tangent transport block}

The induced tangent transport block from the explicit extra \(E/O\) slots is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VEO_active}
\end{equation}

Therefore the local tangent transport densities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:bEO_active}
\end{equation}

So the odd transport density is explicitly nonzero at lowest order whenever
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0,
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0,
\qquad
\cos\theta(\xi)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:odd_density_nonzero_active}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact reduced coefficient sheet}

Define the overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:I3_Ic_defs}
\end{equation}

Then the exact reduced coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, with \(I_{\theta,\cos}=I_c\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_dictionary_alt}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Microscopic one-mediator coefficient point}

At operator level, the one-mediator audit gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_operator_active}
\end{equation}

If the shell basis is canonically normalized so that
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1,
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_canonical_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}
and, in the transport-side canonical explicit normalization where \(J_1\) is absorbed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_canonical_absorbed}
\end{equation}

The same formulas hold for the even slot:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}
}
\label{eq:LambdaE_canonical_absorbed}
\end{equation}
in canonical explicit normalization.

\section{5. Explicit odd coefficient}

Substituting \eqref{eq:LambdaO_operator_active} into \eqref{eq:odd_route_dictionary}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:beta_general_active}
\end{equation}

In the canonical explicit normalization this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c
}
\label{eq:beta_canonical_absorbed}
\end{equation}
if \(J_1\) is absorbed, or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_c
}
\label{eq:beta_canonical_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}
if \(J_1\) is kept explicit.

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,I_c
}
\label{eq:alpha_canonical_absorbed}
\end{equation}
in the same canonical explicit normalization.

\section{6. Resulting reduced PDE}

Therefore the solved lowest-order Branch-B reduced PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

In canonical explicit normalization this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_finalPDE_canonical}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Minimal nonzero criterion}

From \eqref{eq:beta_general_active}, the odd transverse channel is nonzero exactly when
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0,
}
\label{eq:odd_min_nonzero}
\end{equation}
and, if the operator normalization is not absorbed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_OJ_1\neq0.
}
\label{eq:odd_min_nonzero_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}

So the odd channel is no longer waiting on unavailable frozen harmonics.
It is reduced to one coefficient sign/product condition and one geometric overlap condition.

\section{8. Honest relation to the previous mixed odd-active branch}

This move changes the active forward route.

The earlier canonical mixed odd-active branch was structurally closed but still two finite microscopic audits away from a fully populated coefficient point.
By contrast, the explicit odd extra-carrier route already supplies the odd channel at lowest order.

So the honest current forward statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{stop stalling on the unavailable frozen-harmonic }JK\text{ overlap and use the explicit odd extra-carrier route as the active closure route.}
}
\label{eq:odd_active_route_statement}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The correct active forward route is now the explicit odd extra-carrier route.

The \(JK\)-route has already been reduced to a single shell-overlap decision, but that literal sign test still requires unavailable frozen harmonics. By contrast, the explicit odd route is already concrete.

Its odd carrier is
\[
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi,
\]
and the induced tangent transport block is
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
\]

Therefore the reduced coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
with
\[
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

At one-mediator level,
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1,
\]
so in canonical explicit normalization
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
\]

Hence the odd channel is nonzero exactly when
\[
\beta_X\neq0,\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,\qquad
I_c\neq0,
\]
and, in the unabsorbed normalization, also
\[
C_OJ_1\neq0.
\]

So the odd channel is no longer waiting on unavailable frozen harmonics.
The active forward-computable closure route is already explicit.
