\section{Complete Lowest-Order PDE on the Explicit Odd Extra-Carrier Route}

\section{Active branch choice}

We now adopt the explicit odd extra-carrier route as the active forward closure route and fix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O\neq0.
}
\label{eq:gammaO_active_choice}
\end{equation}

If one also wants a nonzero even transverse slot on the same route, one keeps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E\neq0.
}
\label{eq:gammaE_active_choice}
\end{equation}

This does not yet fix the numerical values of \(\gamma_E,\gamma_O\), but it completely fixes the lowest-order coefficient architecture.

\section{1. Exact overlap dictionary}

The reduced coefficient dictionary on the explicit odd extra-carrier route is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_dict_final}
\end{equation}

The geometric overlap integrals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:I3Ic_defs_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. One-mediator coefficient point}

At one-mediator level, the explicit odd/even carrier coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\label{eq:tildeLambdaEO_general}
\end{equation}

In canonical explicit normalization,
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
and if \(J_1\) is absorbed into the coefficient normalization, this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:tildeLambdaEO_canonical}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Final lowest-order coefficient sheet}

Substituting \eqref{eq:tildeLambdaEO_general} into \eqref{eq:odd_route_dict_final}, one gets the general explicit coefficient sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
}
\label{eq:lpar_general_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_general_final}
\end{equation}

In canonical explicit normalization with \(J_1\) absorbed, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_canonical_final}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Complete lowest-order reduced PDE}

The reduced principal symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Therefore the complete lowest-order reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:complete_lowest_order_PDE}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:alpha_beta_general_final}, this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_EJ_1I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_OJ_1I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:complete_lowest_order_PDE_general}
\end{equation}

In canonical explicit normalization with \(J_1\) absorbed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:complete_lowest_order_PDE_canonical}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Dispersion relation}

The resulting dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:dispersion_final}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:alpha_beta_general_final},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{\beta_X^2 I_c^2}{M_X^4}
\Bigl[
(\gamma_E C_EJ_1)^2+(\gamma_O C_OJ_1)^2
\Bigr]
(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:dispersion_general}
\end{equation}

In canonical explicit normalization with \(J_1\) absorbed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{\beta_X^2 I_c^2}{M_X^4}
(\gamma_E^2+\gamma_O^2)\,
(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:dispersion_canonical}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact nonzero conditions}

The longitudinal channel is nonzero iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0.
}
\label{eq:lpar_nonzero_final}
\end{equation}

The even transverse channel is nonzero iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_E\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0,
}
\label{eq:alpha_nonzero_final}
\end{equation}
and, in unabsorbed normalization, also \(C_EJ_1\neq0\).

The odd transverse channel is nonzero iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0,
}
\label{eq:beta_nonzero_final}
\end{equation}
and, in unabsorbed normalization, also \(C_OJ_1\neq0\).

\section{7. Practical final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Complete lowest-order odd-route carrier theorem]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit odd extra-carrier route is adopted;
\item \(\gamma_O\neq0\);
\item \(\lambda_c\neq0\), \(I_3\neq0\), \(I_c\neq0\);
\item \(\beta_X\neq0\);
\item if the operator normalization is unabsorbed, \(C_EJ_1\neq0\) and \(C_OJ_1\neq0\).
\end{enumerate}
Then the reduced lowest-order carrier PDE is exactly \eqref{eq:complete_lowest_order_PDE_general}, and the odd transverse slot is nonzero:
\[
\beta\neq0.
\]
If in addition \(\gamma_E\neq0\), then \(\alpha\neq0\) as well, and the branch carries the full longitudinal-even-odd coefficient triplet at lowest order.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This follows directly from the explicit carrier dictionary \eqref{eq:odd_route_dict_final}, the one-mediator coefficient point \eqref{eq:tildeLambdaEO_general}, and the nonzero conditions \eqref{eq:lpar_nonzero_final}--\eqref{eq:beta_nonzero_final}.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Summary}

Adopting the explicit odd extra-carrier route and choosing \(\gamma_O\neq0\) fixes the complete lowest-order reduced coefficient sheet.

The exact coefficient dictionary is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
with
\[
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

At one-mediator level,
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
\]

Hence the complete lowest-order reduced PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
\]
with
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
\]

In canonical explicit normalization this simplifies to
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
\]

Therefore the odd transverse slot is nonzero exactly when
\[
\beta_X\neq0,\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,\qquad
I_c\neq0,
\]
and, if the normalization is not absorbed, also
\[
C_OJ_1\neq0.
\]

So the odd channel is now closed at complete lowest order on the explicit odd extra-carrier route.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Reference PDE on the Explicit Mixed Transverse Route and Its Matching to the Canonical Mixed Odd-Active Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

The explicit pure-even witness branch
\[
\gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0
\]
is no longer useful for reading the odd coefficient, because it forces
\[
\beta=0.
\]
So the next active branch must satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O\neq0.
}
\label{eq:ref_gammaO_nonzero}
\end{equation}

We therefore adopt the explicit odd extra-carrier route as the reference low-order PDE route.

\section{1. Exact reduced coefficient sheet on the explicit odd route}

The reduced coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c,
}
\label{eq:ref_dict}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:ref_I3Ic}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O.
}
\label{eq:ref_tildeLambda_general}
\end{equation}

In canonical explicit normalization
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:ref_tildeLambda_canonical}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit mixed transverse coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:ref_coeff_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Reference PDE}

The reference reduced symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Hence the reference PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c\,\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c\,\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:ref_PDE}
\end{equation}

The corresponding dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{\beta_X^2 I_c^2}{M_X^4}(\gamma_E^2+\gamma_O^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:ref_dispersion}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Minimal nonzero conditions}

The longitudinal slot is nonzero iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0.
}
\label{eq:ref_long_nonzero}
\end{equation}

The even transverse slot is nonzero iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_E\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0.
}
\label{eq:ref_even_nonzero}
\end{equation}

The odd transverse slot is nonzero iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0.
}
\label{eq:ref_odd_nonzero}
\end{equation}

So the odd route is already closed at lowest order once \(\gamma_O\) is chosen nonzero.

\section{4. Matching to the canonical mixed odd-active branch}

The exact branch-level mixed odd-active coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X T_E\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X T_O\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_mixed_sheet}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit odd route matches the mixed odd-active sheet provided
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:ref_match_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}T_E\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\frac{\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}T_O\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_match_trans}
\end{equation}

In particular, for the canonical mixed odd-active target
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\]
the most natural matched explicit route is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0,
}
\label{eq:ref_gamma_equal}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_gamma_perp_match}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:ref_alpha_beta_equal}
\end{equation}
which is exactly the canonical mixed odd-active transverse sheet.

\section{5. Leading anisotropy ratio}

In the one-mediator truncation the leading anisotropy ratio is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\sqrt{\gamma_E^2+\gamma_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
}
\label{eq:ref_rho}
\end{equation}
in canonical explicit normalization.

For the matched canonical mixed choice \(\gamma_E=\gamma_O=\gamma_\perp\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{3}{32\sqrt2}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{|\gamma_\perp|}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:ref_rho_equal}
\end{equation}

So the explicit odd route not only reproduces the odd channel, but also gives a direct low-order anisotropy formula.

\section{6. Practical final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Reference-PDE theorem on the explicit mixed transverse route]
Assume canonical explicit normalization, and choose
\[
\gamma_O\neq0.
\]
Then the explicit odd extra-carrier route defines the exact lowest-order reduced PDE \eqref{eq:ref_PDE}.

If, in addition,
\[
\lambda_c\neq0,\qquad I_3\neq0,\qquad I_c\neq0,\qquad \beta_X\neq0,
\]
then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,\qquad \beta\neq0.
\]
If also \(\gamma_E\neq0\), then \(\alpha\neq0\) as well.

Finally, if the matching conditions \eqref{eq:ref_match_long}--\eqref{eq:ref_match_trans} hold, then the explicit odd route reproduces the canonical mixed odd-active coefficient sheet.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first part follows directly from \eqref{eq:ref_coeff_sheet}. The second part follows from the nonzero conditions \eqref{eq:ref_long_nonzero}--\eqref{eq:ref_odd_nonzero}. The final statement follows by direct substitution of the matching relations into \eqref{eq:ref_coeff_sheet}.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Summary}

We now fix the explicit odd extra-carrier route as the reference low-order PDE route and choose
\[
\gamma_O\neq0.
\]

In canonical explicit normalization, the exact reduced coefficient sheet is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

Therefore the reference PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c\,\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c\,\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
\]

This route has
\[
\beta\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\beta_X\neq0,\ \gamma_O\neq0,\ I_c\neq0.
\]

Moreover, it matches the canonical mixed odd-active branch provided
\[
\frac{\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}T_E\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\frac{\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}T_O\theta_0\kappa.
\]

For the canonical mixed target \(T_E=T_O=1\), the natural matched choice is
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0,
\]
which reproduces
\[
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa.
\]

So the explicit odd route is now fixed as the reference low-order PDE route, and it can be matched directly onto the canonical mixed odd-active coefficient sheet.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Fixing the Current Reference PDE by the Symmetric Mixed Transverse Choice}

\section{Reference branch choice}

We fix the active branch parameters by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0.
}
\label{eq:ref_gamma_perp_choice}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal symmetric mixed transverse choice that keeps both transverse channels alive and matches naturally onto the canonical mixed odd-active target.

\section{1. Exact coefficient sheet on the explicit odd route}

The explicit odd extra-carrier route has the exact reduced dictionary
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:ref_coeff_dict}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level, in canonical explicit normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:ref_tildeLambda_can}
\end{equation}

Therefore under \eqref{eq:ref_gamma_perp_choice},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:ref_coeff_sheet_perp}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta.
}
\label{eq:ref_alpha_equals_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Reference PDE in the original transverse coordinates}

The reduced symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Using \eqref{eq:ref_coeff_sheet_perp}, the reference PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:ref_PDE_original}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Rotated transverse form}

Because \(\alpha=\beta\), introduce the rotated transverse coordinates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:ref_qcoords}
\end{equation}

Then the symbol becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(q_1\sigma_1+q_2\sigma_2\bigr),
}
\label{eq:ref_symbol_rotated}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
=
\sqrt2\,\alpha
=
-\sqrt2\,\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:ref_vperp}
\end{equation}

Hence the reference PDE takes the isotropic transverse form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:ref_PDE_rotated}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact matching to the canonical mixed odd-active branch}

The branch-level canonical mixed odd-active sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_mixed_target}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit odd route matches the canonical mixed odd-active target iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:ref_long_match}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_trans_match}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:ref_trans_match},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:ref_alpha_beta_matched}
\end{equation}
so the transverse reference sheet coincides exactly with the canonical mixed odd-active branch.

\section{5. Dispersion relation}

The corresponding dispersion relation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
2\left(\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}\right)^2 I_c^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:ref_dispersion_original}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
\bigl(v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}\bigr)^2(q_1^2+q_2^2).
}
\label{eq:ref_dispersion_rotated}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Reference-branch fixation theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Current reference-PDE fixation theorem]
Assume canonical explicit normalization and choose
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0.
\]
Then the explicit odd extra-carrier route defines the reference lowest-order reduced PDE
\eqref{eq:ref_PDE_rotated} with coefficient sheet \eqref{eq:ref_coeff_sheet_perp}.

If, in addition,
\[
\lambda_c\neq0,\qquad
I_3\neq0,\qquad
I_c\neq0,\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\]
then all three reduced channels are nonzero:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
\alpha\neq0,\qquad
\beta\neq0.
\]

Finally, if the matching relations \eqref{eq:ref_long_match} and \eqref{eq:ref_trans_match} hold,
then the reference PDE reproduces the canonical mixed odd-active coefficient sheet exactly.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Directly from \eqref{eq:ref_coeff_sheet_perp}, \eqref{eq:ref_PDE_rotated}, and the matching relations.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Summary}

We now fix the current reference branch by
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0.
\]

On the explicit odd extra-carrier route, this gives the exact lowest-order coefficient sheet
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

Hence the current reference PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
\]
with
\[
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
=
-\sqrt2\,\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

This reference route matches the canonical mixed odd-active branch exactly if
\[
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Therefore the explicit odd extra-carrier route is now fixed as the current reference low-order PDE route, and it reproduces the canonical mixed odd-active transverse sheet after the matching is imposed.

\section{PROJECT: TECT --- Master Contents for Continuation (Reference PDE Fixed and Mixed-Branch Matching Stage)}

\section{Current Stage}

}
\end{equation}
while

and the remaining task is to match the reference route onto that target branch and continue the finite coefficient extraction.

The sharp current separation is:

\boxed{
\text{Reference route: explicit odd extra-carrier route (forward-computable now),}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Target route: canonical mixed odd-active branch (structurally closed, two finite audits remain).}
}
\end{equation}

\section{What is already fixed}

The canonical mixed odd-active target branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2}.
}
\end{equation}

Its exact reduced branch-level coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the target mixed branch is no longer waiting on branch-choice logic.
What remains there is only microscopic coefficient population.

\section{Why the active forward route changed}

The earlier \(JK\)-route for the odd slot was reduced to a finite shell-overlap decision, but its literal sign test still requires unavailable frozen harmonics.
Therefore the correct forward move was to stop stalling there and switch to the explicit odd extra-carrier route.

The decisive explicit odd slot is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\end{equation}

Its induced tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\end{equation}

Hence the local odd density is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
}
\end{equation}
so the odd channel is explicitly realizable at lowest order once
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0.
\]

\section{Current reference branch choice}

From now on, the current reference branch is fixed by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal symmetric mixed-transverse choice that keeps both transverse channels alive and matches naturally to the target condition
\[
T_E=T_O=1.
\]

\section{Reference low-order coefficient dictionary}

The explicit odd-route reduced coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_dict}
\end{equation}

The overlap integrals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:MC_I3Ic}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level, in canonical explicit normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:MC_tildeLambda}
\end{equation}

Under the fixed reference choice \(\gamma_E=\gamma_O=\gamma_\perp\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_coeff_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{Current reference PDE}

The current reference reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_PDE}
\end{equation}

Introducing rotated transverse coordinates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2},
}
\end{equation}
the same reference PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_PDE_rot}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
=
-\sqrt2\,\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:MC_vperp_ref}
\end{equation}

The corresponding dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
2\left(\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}\right)^2 I_c^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_disp}
\end{equation}

\section{Reference-route nonzero conditions}

The reference route has

and
\begin{equation}

So the current reference branch is nondegenerate as soon as

\qquad
